Land Value Tax Collection Begins on Schedule in the City 153

Deadline is Two Months from the First of Next Month

The Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating that the first installment of the provisional land value tax for the 24th year of the Republic of China, which should be levied on Districts 1 to 7 of the South Shanghai District, Districts 1 to 4 of the Fahua District, District 1 of the Pusong District, and Districts 5, 6, and 8 of the Yinxiang District, is scheduled to begin on March 1 of this year. The deadline for payment is two months from the date of collection, ending on April 30 of this year. Those whose land is in the South Shanghai District should bring the previous receipt and pay at the Municipal South Tax Collection Office of the Bureau on Maojia Lane in the South City. Those in the Fahua and Pusong Districts should bring the previous receipt and pay at the Municipal West Tax Collection Office of the Bureau at the intersection of Robison Road and Binlang Road. Those in the Yinxiang District should bring the previous receipt and pay at the Municipal North Tax Collection Office of the Bureau on Datong Road in Zhabei. Those who fail to pay within the deadline will have their land income extracted and sold for compensation according to Article 8 of the Provisional Regulations for the Collection of Land Value Tax and according to the years in arrears, in order to comply with the regulations and emphasize tax collection. In addition to reporting to the Municipal Government and sending notices, this announcement is hereby issued so that taxpayers are all informed and must pay on time without delay, lest they incur punishment. If any notices have not yet been received, they should, within the deadline, state the location of the land, the diagram number, and the current residence address or mailing address and come to the Bureau to declare so that a duplicate can be found and sent. Pay with the previous receipt, do not delay!

Ministry of Industry Approves Chamber of Commerce to Establish Large Factories in Beiping 154

A Letter Has Been Sent to the Executive Yuan's Office in Beiping for Handling

Convenient for Telephone Users in the South City to Send Telegrams 155

To be Implemented from March 1

In order to make it convenient for users of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau to send telegrams, the Ministry of Communications has promulgated "Measures for Shanghai Telephone Bureau Users to Transmit Telegrams by Telephone," which will be implemented from March 1 of this year. After receiving the order, the two bureaus of Shanghai Telephone and Telegraph have prepared to implement it as scheduled and have notified users of the measures yesterday. The following is a summary of the measures: (1) All users of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications (hereinafter referred to as "users"), whether in the South City, Longhua, Zhabei, Pudong, or the city center, may transmit telegrams by telephone in accordance with these measures. (2) Users who wish to transmit telegrams by telephone should follow the following procedures: (a) Call telephones No. 21193 or 21194 in the South City (these telephones are located in the Republic of China Road Receiving and Dispatching Office of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau); (b) After the user hears the reply from the Telegraph Bureau, they must report the telephone number and account name clearly (the Telegraph Bureau may inquire about the sender's name, position, or other matters to prove that they are indeed the user themselves or someone who can be held responsible. If the Telegraph Bureau considers it suspicious, it may ask the sender to write the telegram themselves and send it to the bureau for transmission); (c) Hang up the telephone and wait for the Telegraph Bureau personnel to notify them to send the telegram; (d) When the Telegraph Bureau personnel call the original number again to ask for the telephone number and account name, the user must repeat it. If it matches, they can start sending the telegram; (e) Users who send Chinese telegrams, whether clear or coded, must translate them into code in advance. When sending the telegram, they should read out the code word by word on the telephone so that the Telegraph Bureau personnel can record it. However, in order to avoid mishearing, the code should be read out in the following manner when necessary (reading method omitted); (f) Users who transmit foreign language telegrams must read out the letters one by one. When necessary, the letters should be read out in the following manner (reading method omitted); (g) After the user has finished transmitting the telegram, the Telegraph Bureau personnel will repeat it once. If the proofreading is correct, the recorded telegram will be sent out by machine and a copy will be prepared, stating the amount of telegram fee to be collected (to be collected in total at the end of the month) and delivered to the original sender by the deliveryman to be reviewed, signed, and stamped in person, and then returned to the Telegraph Bureau by the original deliveryman for safekeeping as proof. If the sender finds any errors, they should immediately notify the Telegraph Bureau by telephone to send a public telegram to correct them. The fee for this public telegram will still be charged according to regulations. The procedure for reviewing telegram copies must be handled quickly to avoid delaying the deliveryman's time. If the sender is out, their family or entrusted person may sign and stamp to be responsible for the review or collect it on their behalf and leave it for the Telegraph Bureau to send a deliveryman to pick it up the next day; (3) After a telegram transmitted by telephone reaches its destination, if the recipient has any questions and calls to inquire, the Telegraph Bureau should first check and correct the telegram base received on the telephone. If there are no errors in the telegram base check, the sender should be notified by telephone to recheck. If there are errors, a charged public telegram should be used to correct them. The fee for this charged public telegram will still be charged according to regulations; (4) After the user has finished transmitting the telegram or the charged public telegram, they may ask how much the total telegram fee is. The Telegraph Bureau personnel should immediately calculate and reply. If the sender does not inquire, the Telegraph Bureau personnel will not notify them on the telephone in order to avoid delaying the time of sending the telegram; (5) The telegram fees for telegrams transmitted by telephone will be recorded by the Telegraph Bureau at any time, and at the end of the month, the Telegraph Bureau will fill out a bill according to the number of each user and send it to the Telephone Bureau. The Telephone Bureau will then collect the telegram fees from the users on behalf of the Telegraph Bureau. If there are any arrears, the Telephone Bureau will handle them in the same way as the arrears of telephone charges; (6) The Telegraph Bureau will not collect a deposit from users who transmit these accounting telegrams, but the deposit paid by the user to the Telephone Bureau will also serve as a deposit; (7) If the total telegram fee payable by a user who sends more telegrams reaches 50 yuan by any day of the month, the Telegraph Bureau should immediately notify the user to register directly with the Telegraph Bureau in accordance with the Measures for the Sending and Receiving of Telegrams by Urban Telephones promulgated by the Ministry of Communications and deposit the telegram fee in advance before continuing to send telegrams; (8) The method of transmitting telegrams by telephone is temporarily limited to ordinary telegrams, urgent telegrams, and social telegrams sent to various places in the country. Other types of telegrams are not applicable; (9) Telephones installed in institutions, groups, schools, hotels, teahouses, restaurants, theaters, bathhouses, and other public places are not subject to these regulations unless the user notifies the Telephone Bureau in writing that they are willing to transmit telegrams in accordance with these measures and is responsible for paying the telegram fees; (10) These measures do not apply to public telephones or telephone users in the concessions, or to users in arrears with telephone charges (the Telephone Bureau will notify the Telegraph Bureau at any time); (11) These measures will be implemented on a trial basis from March 1, 24th year of the Republic of China.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Beiping Chamber of Commerce requesting that it be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry to establish large factories in Beiping in order to benefit industrial construction and that it should consistently advocate for this. The Chamber cabled the Ministry for action last month. The Chamber received a reply from the Ministry of Industry yesterday, which is recorded as follows: "I received the cable on behalf of you. This case was previously submitted to the Ministry by the Beiping Chamber of Commerce. I believe that the Ministry of Industry, in order to develop large factories to benefit people's livelihood, approved the promulgation of the Measures for the Establishment of People's Livelihood Factories in Counties and Cities in September of the 21st year and issued a circular to the provincial and municipal governments in March of the 22nd year to implement the measures in accordance with the aforementioned measures. The request of the Chamber of Commerce is intended to develop local industries, which is in line with the main purpose of the previous order." A separate letter was sent to the Executive Yuan's Political Affairs Committee in Beiping and the Beiping Municipal Government to consider and handle the matter and to notify all parties concerned.

Xingsafo Arrives in Shanghai for a Medical Examination 156

Personnel Sent by the Panchen Lama's Office in Beijing Accompany Him to Shanghai

Xingsa Bandan Dafo, a representative of the Qinghai Mongolian and Tibetan people, arrived in Shanghai at 2:30 PM on the 8th on the Beijing-Zhabei train for a medical examination. After that, he will go north to Qinghai to welcome the Panchen Lama.

Pinghan Railway and China Merchants Bureau Handling Combined Water-Land Through Transport 158

First Batch of Goods to Shanghai Arriving Tomorrow

Northbound Goods to be Loaded Tomorrow and the Day After

The State-Run China Merchants Bureau and the Pinghan Railway are handling combined water-land through transport to facilitate the transportation of goods. Details are as follows:

Notice of Through Transport: The Pinghan Railway China Merchants Bureau's through transport notice states that, in order to facilitate transportation for merchants, the two bureaus have decided to implement combined water-land through transport of goods from January 11th of this year. All goods transported to and from the following stations and ports, regardless of whether they are military or otherwise, may be delivered to the railway station or shipping bureau for through transport and delivery. For detailed methods, please inquire at the Pinghan Railway Traffic Office and various stations, or the China Merchants General Bureau and various port branches. The following are the convenience points for combined water-land through transport of goods, and the stations and ports where through transport is implemented: (1) Through transport freight: the railway bureau charges according to the current freight rates, and the shipping bureau calculates and charges according to the current water freight rates. Payment methods are divided into two types: prepayment and payment on arrival. Prepayment is collected in advance at the time of shipment, while payment on arrival is paid by the owner upon arrival of the goods. The shipper is free to choose between prepayment and payment on arrival. (2) For through transport goods passing through Hankou or other ports, the procedures for loading, unloading, customs declaration, and inspection will be handled by the railway or shipping bureau. The taxes to be paid will also be advanced by the shipping bureau and collected from the consignee upon arrival of the goods, without any additional handling fees.

Departure Stations and Ports: The departure stations specified by the two routes are Xiaogan, Huayuan, Xiaojiagang, Guangshui, Xinyang, Changtaiguan, Mingguang, Xinan, Dian, Queshan, Zhumadian, Suiping, Xiping, Yancheng, Linying, Xuzhou, Heshangqiao, Xinzheng, Xuedian, Xiezhuang, Zhengzhou, North Bank of the Yellow River, Xinxiang, Weihui, Tangyin, Baoliansi, Zhangde, Matouzhen, Handan, Shunde, Shijiazhuang, Baoding, Liangxiang. The arrival stations for through transport are Xiaogan, Huayuan, Guangshui, Xinyang, Mingguang, Zhumadian, Xiping, Yancheng, Xuzhou, Zhengzhou, Xinxiang, Zhangde, Handan, Shunde, Shijiazhuang, Baoding, Fengtai, Qianmen. The departure and arrival ports for through transport are Shanghai, Nanjing, Anqing, Wuhu, Jiujiang.

First Batch of Goods: The first batch of through transport goods, totaling more than 2,000 tons, was loaded onto the Jianghua轮 in Hankou on the 31st and shipped to Shanghai. Most of the goods are medicinal materials. However, the Jianghua轮 ran aground en route and will not arrive in Shanghai until tomorrow. The first batch of northbound goods from Shanghai will be loaded onto the Jiangda轮, which will depart tomorrow, and the Jianghua轮, which will depart the day after.

New Measures for Railway Transportation of Copper Coins, Cash Coins, and Copper Ingots

Ministry of Railways Instructions 159

The two railway administrations received Instruction No. 399 from the Ministry of Railways, stating: This Ministry has previously received a consultation from the Ministry of Finance stating that inferior copper coins are rampant on the market and should be strictly prohibited. Please instruct all railway bureaus to strictly inspect and enforce the "Measures for the Transportation of Copper Coins by State-Owned Railways" to confiscate them and prevent private transportation to emphasize the ban. After verification by this Ministry, the original "Measures for the Transportation of Copper Coins, Cash Coins, and Copper Ingots by State-Owned Railways" did not specify the confiscation of privately transported copper coins without a license, the reporting procedures for the confiscation of privately transported copper coins, the reward methods for those who discover privately transported copper coins, and the conversion rates for copper coins worth 50, 100, and 200. Therefore, difficulties inevitably arise during implementation. This Ministry has revised and supplemented the original measures and has obtained the approval of the Ministry of Finance after consultation. In addition to the general order, a copy of these revised measures is urgently copied and issued to the road, so that it can be followed and ordered to strictly check the necessity of the order. The bureau has instructed the traffic office to follow the order.

Revised Measures 160

Revised Measures for the Transportation of Copper Coins, Cash Coins, and Copper Ingots by State-Owned Railways: (1) Passengers traveling by train who carry single copper coins (i.e., ten-wen copper coins) within 2,000 pieces, or double copper coins (i.e., twenty-wen copper coins) within 1,000 pieces, or cash coins within 5,000 pieces, are exempt from freight charges. (2) Passengers who carry single copper coins exceeding 2,000 but not exceeding 20,000 pieces, or double copper coins exceeding 1,000 but not exceeding 10,000 pieces, or cash coins exceeding 5,000 but not exceeding 50,000 pieces, shall pay freight charges and be issued a ticket for shipment. If there is any concealment or private transportation, a fine of ten times the freight shall be imposed and released in accordance with Article 39 of the General Rules for Freight Car Transportation. If no one claims the goods, they shall be confiscated. (3) Passengers who carry single copper coins exceeding 20,000 pieces, or double copper coins exceeding 10,000 pieces, or cash coins exceeding 50,000 pieces, shall hold a passport issued by the provincial, municipal, or county government for travel within the province, or a passport issued by the Ministry of Finance for transport to other provinces. Both shall be presented to the station for verification at the time of reporting for shipment and payment of fees. If privately transported copper coins or cash coins without a license are found, they shall be detained in full and reported to the bureau. In addition to the recovery of the supplementary freight charge, all shall be confiscated. If no one claims the goods, they shall be confiscated in full. (4) When shipping copper coins or cash coins with a passport, the ordinary full price shall be charged. If there is any private transportation, even with a passport, a fine of ten times the freight shall be imposed and released in accordance with Article 39 of the General Rules for Freight Car Transportation. (5) Railway employees traveling to and from their own lines are limited to carrying 1,000 single copper coins or 500 double copper coins. As for cash coins, which are no longer widely used, they are limited to 100 pieces and are exempt from freight charges. If this number is exceeded, regardless of the amount, all shall be confiscated. (6) Privately transported copper coins or cash coins confiscated in accordance with Articles 2, 3, and 5 of these measures shall be handed over by the stationmaster to the accounting office. The railway bureau shall allocate 20% of the confiscated copper coins or cash coins as a bonus for the personnel who discovered them. If discovered by police officers, the police section shall forward them to the stationmaster for reporting and submission, and report to the relevant police authorities for verification. (7) When passengers carry copper coins, if they are various copper coins worth 50, 100, or 200, they shall be converted and calculated according to the number of single copper coins. (8) Copper ingots are allowed to be transported by rail upon payment of fees, but false reporting or concealment is not allowed. If they are transported privately by other means without formal reporting, they shall be handled in accordance with Article 39 of the Transportation Regulations upon discovery. (9) Privately transported copper ingots may be confiscated by the railway if no one claims them upon discovery. (10) The above measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Chinese Cotton Mill's Opinions on Revised Import Taxes 162

Submitted by the Executive Yuan to the Ministries of Finance and Industry for Verification

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Chinese Cotton Mill Association stated that the sales of Chinese cotton yarn are declining daily. Unless costs are reduced or import taxes on foreign cotton cloth are increased to remedy the situation, it will become increasingly precarious. It has recently been heard that the Ministry of Finance intends to revise import tariffs and has recorded the revisions. The Legislative Yuan will soon review them. Therefore, a special request has been submitted to the Executive Yuan, requesting that the situation of Chinese cotton yarn be carefully considered when revising import tariffs and that cotton cloth import tariffs be appropriately increased to provide relief. The Executive Yuan yesterday ordered the Ministries of Finance and Industry to jointly verify the matter.

Drought Relief Charity Association Investigates Disastrous Conditions in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces

Report from Zhang Jun 163

The Drought Relief Charity Association of Various Provinces, having received reports on the disaster situation in various counties from Zhang Lanping, Director of Inspection and Relief in Jiangsu Province, states the following: (1) Letters have been received from Qin Zhujiang and others, town chiefs of Shipu and Sheshan in Jiangning County, stating that disaster victims are suffering from hunger, cold, and starvation, requesting methods of relief. Deputy Director Li Tianzhen has been instructed to go to the area to investigate the veracity of the reported disaster situation. Further measures will be proposed and reported upon receipt of his reply. (2) A large letter has been received, along with a letter from the Wujin County Disaster Relief Committee appealing for emergency relief in the disaster area and a list of the drought situation. Having read them all, it is confirmed that relief is necessary. However, the disaster area is so vast, the number of disaster victims is so large, and the disaster situation is so dire that the Association cannot handle it independently. Concrete measures by the county or joint cooperation with other charitable organizations are necessary for the Association to conduct inspection and relief. (3) In the eighth and ninth districts of Jiangdu, in addition to the report from representative Wang Shaohe, Lanping also sent people for secret investigation. It is estimated that there are more than 120,000 disaster victims. The poorest account for 70-80% of the population. There are tragic cases of children being drowned and couples committing suicide. However, the county must have its own plan before the Association can proceed. Otherwise, with severe disaster and meager funds, we dare not act rashly. (4) Zheng Shouchang, Executive Director of Lishui County, telegraphed that disaster victims in various townships of the county have exhausted all livestock and are surviving by collecting aquatic plants from the river. Deaths are seen daily. It is difficult to fully describe the misery. The previously allocated relief funds are insufficient for distribution, requesting that the conference increase the amount. Lanping intends to wait until they have reached a certain stage before determining how much to allocate. The Director of Inspection and Relief of the Association must investigate the actual situation of disaster relief in various counties and begin to plan. Although it is difficult to provide comprehensive relief with great disaster and meager funds, we must uphold our conscience, do our best, adhere to the principle of saving the dying but not the poor, strictly investigate and implement relief, save one person and save one life, and ensure that relief funds are not wasted.

Lawyers Association Asks Court to Pay Attention to the Dignity of the Court 166

Not Just Because of the Ke Yinghao Case

The Shanghai Lawyers Association sent another letter to the Shanghai First Special District Court regarding the Ke Yinghao case, in which he shouted in court and insulted lawyer Zhu Sifu, a member of the association. The letter stated: According to the letter from member Zhu Sifu, regarding the case in which member representative Liu Yide's rental office sued Min Ke Yinghao, who lived at No. 5, Ping Le Lane, Xizang Road, for owing more than 1,000 yuan in rent, when the judge of the First Special Court, Luo Chongtai, convened a hearing in the Civil Court No. 7 on December 10, the member representative and the party concerned appeared in court, and Ke Yinghao also appeared in court. He stated that he was from Shanghang County, Fujian Province, and that in the eighth year of the Republic, Ji, stationed in Japan, applied to the Ministry of Interior to renounce his nationality. In the ninth year of the Republic, he formally became a Japanese national and was therefore not subject to the jurisdiction of the national court. At the same time, he submitted a certificate of Japanese citizenship as proof. At that time, the member argued that, according to Article 11 of the Nationality Law, the renunciation of nationality by a person must have a certificate of renunciation of nationality from the Ministry of Interior of the country in order to be valid. Ke Yinghao only submitted a certificate of citizenship, which cannot be recognized as Japanese nationality under the law. Unexpectedly, at this time, Ke Yinghao stepped down from the defendant's seat in the courtroom and strode in front of the judge. Although the judge stopped him, it was ineffective. He even vented his anger on the member, raised his fist to strike the member. Fortunately, the bailiff stopped him, avoiding abuse. However, Ke cursed the member in Mandarin, saying that he had to beat him. His voice was loud and menacing. Judge Luo then adjourned the case to investigate his nationality with the Ministry of Interior and left the court. Ke was still unwilling and waited outside the courtroom, wanting to get the member and be satisfied. After being informed, the member declared this situation to the court at that time, and in order to avoid his violence, he had to temporarily avoid it in the court. After a long time, Ke left the court. This is the situation at the time. A lawyer only knows to handle litigation on behalf of the party concerned according to law. If the defendant has any defense, he can make a proper statement to the court in accordance with legal principles, and cannot vent his anger on the lawyer. Now Ke Yinghao relied on his Japanese nationality and dared to act arbitrarily in the dignified court, and even wanted to beat the member in court. After leaving the court, he waited outside the door for a long time. Checking the order of the court, people of all nationalities should strictly abide by it. If there is any violation, the judge can take him into custody and send him to the consulate of the country for investigation. Moreover, it is not yet possible to prove whether Ke Yinghao has actually become a Japanese national before the Ministry of Interior has replied. He dared to be so violent. If he is formally a Japanese national, I don't know how tyrannical he will be. Ke Yinghao's behavior not only insulted the members, but also damaged the prestige of the Chinese court. Insulting members is a trivial matter, disregarding the solemnity of the national court is a major event. If he is not severely punished, this kind of event will follow one after another. I have to report urgently. For this reason, I especially ask Jun Hui to forward it to the Procuratorate of the First Special District Court, quickly investigate and detain Ke Yinghao. If the Ministry of Interior replies in the future and proves that he has indeed renounced his nationality, he will be sent to the Japanese consulate for punishment. If it is found that he is not Japanese, he will be severely punished according to the law to warn the violent and respect the law. According to the previous time, the association had detailed the facts of Zhu's member being insulted by Ke Yinghao in court, and sent a letter to Junyuan for correction. Nai Du Junyuan believed that it was based on hearsay and did not conform to the facts. It also stated that maintaining the dignity of the court, Junyuan was more concerned than any other party. No matter what country the offender was, the presiding judge had already dealt with him according to the law, without waiting for him to take any further illegal actions before correcting him. Today, the statement made by Zhu's association seems to be not much different from the rumors in the newspaper. The association deeply feels that the presiding judge at the time had not fulfilled his duty to handle the case according to law, and it is difficult to guarantee that the same kind of event will not happen in the future. There is still a need to request correction. It was discussed and decided at the 188th joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Association that another letter should be sent to the Shanghai First Special District Court for correction. It should be noted that maintaining the dignity of the court is the authority of Junyuan, and the association does not need to make a vain request. However, Fayuan is the place where Chinese and foreigners watch, and in the past year, there have been occasional deviations in the solemn place of the court, such as the gathering of hooligans in the Ji Buddha case, shouting slogans, and the member Cai Yicheng of the Samsung Yarn Factory being openly thrown feces. The association regards all these things as extremely regrettable. Therefore, dare to state its stupidity and use it for fodder. I want Junyuan to be humble and will not consider it a third violation. Shanghai First Special District Court, Shen Junru, Chen Tingrui, Wang Weizhen, Standing Committee Members of the Shanghai Lawyers Association, respectfully.

Shanghai Municipal Council Changes Employment Method for Foreign Staff 168

Focus on Local Recruitment

In Order to Save Expenses

Since 1931, the Municipal Council has changed its employment of staff to a letter of appointment. There are two types of appointment letters: A, meaning recruited from abroad, and L, meaning recruited locally. Staff with the L designation do not have the right to a half-year leave after five years, nor do they have travel expenses for employment or departure. In recent years, there have been as many as 140 foreign staff employed with the L designation, saving the bureau a lot of expenses. In special circumstances, L-designated staff may be changed to A, but this has not yet been implemented. The Chief of Finance has recently drafted several measures to achieve a uniform intention in thrift. The main points of the measures are as follows: 1. In the future, all foreign staff, regardless of where they are recruited, will be L-designated staff and must serve for at least five years. 2. If the service period is long, or the position has a specialized nature, or it is permanently needed, the staff member may be allowed to change to A-designated treatment. 3. Experts holding special positions are not subject to the restrictions of Article 1. 4. Those recruited from abroad or those recruited as British military personnel to serve in the police department will receive the same treatment as those who hold positions in other departments, but these personnel will receive the benefit of exchange rate preferences when they are dismissed. 5. Japanese and Indian personnel will be handled in accordance with the new regulations. These measures have been agreed to by the heads of various departments and have been submitted to the Board of Directors through the Appointments Committee. The Board of Directors has adopted them in principle on the 7th of this month. As for what kind of positions will be treated as A-designated in the future, it will be determined again.

He possesses deep insights into gastroenterology and pediatric infectious diseases, often achieving remarkable cures. His dedication to research is truly admirable. It is expected that upon his return, he will make significant contributions to the field of medicine.

Guests Fill the Hall, Flower Baskets Abound

Grand Ceremony for Xiong and Mao's Wedding 171

The Groom Radiates Happiness and Energy

The Bride Adorned with Light Makeup, Poised and Elegant

Couplets of All Kinds, Clever and Witty Sayings

Former Premier Xiong Xiling, now sixty-six years old, remarried yesterday at 3 PM at Moore Memorial Church to Ms. Mao Yanwen, a returned student from the United States and a university professor. Ms. Mao is thirty-nine years old. The marriage between an older man and a younger woman has become a widely circulated story. Many prominent figures in Shanghai attended to offer their congratulations, causing traffic jams and creating a grand spectacle. The wedding ceremony is detailed below. Xiong and Mao (Photo by Xu Tianzhang)

Guests Fill the Hall 172

Attendees at yesterday's wedding included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Central Committee members Li Shizeng, Qin Zhen, He Yaozu, Li Sihao, Gao Lu, Tao Jiayao, Xu Shiying, Liang Hongzhi, Xue Dubi, Zhang Shizhao, Zhang Gongquan, Chen Guangfu, Hu Bijang, Qian Xinzhi, Zhang Shouyong, Wu Yunzhai, Tang Shoumin, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Yiting, Wang Xiaolai, Li Zushen, Chen Shuqing, Lin Kanghou, Zhao Jinqing, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Chu [blank], Zhang Yuanji, Feng Gengguang, Pan Gongzhan, Wang Boqi, Yan Duhe, Mei Lanfang, and over a thousand others. Dong Xianguang, Guo Dehua, Zhao Shuyong, and others served as hosts.

Flower Baskets Abound 173

Moore Memorial Church is the most magnificent church in Shanghai. The pulpit is semicircular with three tiers, each adorned with cypress leaves and filled with flower baskets presented by various circles. The flowers bloomed, resembling a flower array. There were no less than one hundred and ten baskets in total. The ones sent by Feng Yuxiang and Mei Lanfang were particularly eye-catching. The highest point was the place for musical performances. The religious atmosphere blended with the fragrance of flowers, making the hall feel even more sublime and sweet.

The New Couple's Demeanor 174

Yesterday at 2:30 PM, Mr. Xiong arrived at the church before the bride and sat in the first seat in the first row of the audience. He wore a blue robe and black mandarin jacket. His hair had been meticulously groomed, and he greeted the arriving guests warmly with handshakes. He radiated happiness and energy, looking no older than forty. At 3 PM sharp, the bride, Ms. Mao, arrived gracefully with her bridesmaids. The bride wore a tiara, a white veil, a white satin dress, and silver-gray high heels. She was fashionably dressed, wearing gold-rimmed glasses and light makeup, displaying unmatched elegance. As the church organ played, the ceremony began.

Simple and Solemn Ceremony 175

The ceremony began at 3:10 PM. The officiating pastor, Zhu Baoyuan, stood in front of the pulpit. The bride and groom stood before the altar. The male bridesmaid was Mao Fangmei, the bride's cousin, and the female bridesmaid was Mrs. Zhu Tingqi. After the music ended, the pastor recited a sacred verse. Due to church etiquette, there was no applause or cheering. The couple and the guests listened reverently to the sacred words in a calm and peaceful atmosphere. After the verse, the music resumed. The couple stood facing each other, holding hands. The pastor asked the bride and groom if they were willing to be married. After each stated their willingness and exchanged rings, the ceremony concluded in fifteen minutes. The couple retreated hand-in-hand, and then the guests slowly dispersed. The Christian ceremony was simple and solemn.

Collection of Witty Couplets 176

After the ceremony, Mr. Xiong accompanied the bride and bridesmaids to rest for a while, awaiting the evening banquet at the New Asia Restaurant on North Sichuan Road. The banquet was held on the ground floor of the New Asia Restaurant, with many congratulatory banners hanging on the walls, featuring witty couplets. Several of the most poignant and humorous couplets are transcribed below. A student named Liu Fuxuan wrote: "Phoenixes fly together, an auspicious omen for the 'Xiong' dream. Zithers and lutes sound in harmony, composing 'Mao' poems." Zheng Hongnian wrote: "Surrounded by children and grandchildren, welcoming a new mother; enjoying the pleasure, watching the old husband." Feng Chen Zhaoyu wrote: "Old classmates become new aunts; old uncles become older brothers-in-law." The ninety-six-year-old Ma Liang wrote: "Blessings arrive late in life, forming a happy couple. Spring arrives earlier than the day, a celestial marriage." Zhang Shizhao wrote: "Seeking a phoenix in the Azure Cave of Several Peaks; leading a phoenix to the Vermilion Mountain of Ten Thousand Miles." He also noted: "Zhang Yu's poem: 'Before which peak is the azure cave? In what year did the phoenix seek its mate here?' In the first month of Yi Hai, Bing Lao and Ms. Mao Yanwen were married at Moore Memorial Church in Shanghai, fulfilling the meaning of this poem. Therefore, I have combined it with a line from Han Yu's poem to create a congratulatory couplet, hoping for the new sounds of young phoenixes and looking forward to the blossoming of flowers. Friends and relatives from home and abroad, let us all listen attentively. Zhao also dares to write these words." Another person, calling himself the seventy-two-year-old Cui Nengyue, wrote a couplet that was particularly well-crafted: "Old husband, sixty-six; new wife, thirty-three; old husband and new wife, ninety-nine. White hair in pairs, rosy cheeks in pairs, white hair and rosy cheeks, eyebrows aligned."

A Glimpse into the Honeymoon Suite 177

Mr. Xiong's new residence is at 1331 Route Lafayette, Apt. 36 on the third floor of the Citibank Apartments. It consists of one reception room, two bedrooms, one kitchen, and two bathrooms, with a monthly rent of about two hundred yuan. When the reporter knocked on the door, a male servant greeted them. The furnishings in the room were all provided by the landlord. His personal belongings were mostly gifts from relatives and friends or items that were borrowed. On the walls, besides the couplet by the ninety-six-year-old Ma Xiangbo and the congratulatory poems from Xiong's nephew Zhu Jingnong and others, there were also four paintings of beautiful women by Yun Shouping, titled "Talented Women Writing Books, Beautifully Painting Eyebrows, Playing the Xiao to Attract the Phoenix, Celestial Couple on the Blue Bridge," which were particularly valuable. There were also one or two famous Western paintings. Yesterday at 5 PM, the couple briefly hosted guests at the New Asia Restaurant and then took a night train to Hangzhou to enjoy their honeymoon.

Sanctions for Child Abuse 186

Article 286 of the New Criminal Law Provides Explicit Punishment

Child Welfare Organizations Can Also Report to the Prosecutor

In June 1934, the China Child Welfare Association, based on reliable reports, handled the case of Zhang Aizhen, a Shanghai dancer, abusing her six-year-old adopted daughter, Zhang Xiaobao. Although the injuries were verified in court, the judge, based on Article 293 of the Criminal Law, which requires prosecution upon complaint, and after questioning Xiaobao herself, who was too young and ignorant to express a desire to prosecute, ruled that the case was inadmissible and returned the victim to her abuser. The Association believed that this situation was frequently encountered in society. If the judgment was considered inappropriate, then Article 293 of the Criminal Law clearly stipulated that prosecution required a complaint. If the judgment was considered appropriate, what would become of the abused children? Therefore, in July, the Association specifically petitioned the Judicial Yuan to allow domestic child welfare organizations to have the right to prosecute on behalf of children when necessary, so as to remedy the difficulties in the Criminal Law and to impose appropriate sanctions on those who abused children and cunningly played with the law. The Association then received a reply from the Judicial Yuan, stating that since the matter concerned legislation, it had been forwarded to the Criminal Law Review Committee of the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. According to recent news, the China Child Welfare Association received another reply from the Judicial Yuan yesterday (February 9), stating that based on the Criminal Law Review Committee's deliberation, Article 286 of the New Criminal Law already had concrete provisions for punishing child abuse, and there seemed to be no need to enact a separate right to prosecute on behalf of children. Article 286 of the New Criminal Law stipulates: "Anyone who abuses a man or woman under the age of sixteen or uses other methods to hinder their physical development shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to five years, detention, or a fine of up to five hundred yuan. Anyone who commits the preceding crime with the intent to profit shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than five years and may also be fined up to one thousand yuan." The punishment does not require prosecution upon complaint. The prosecutor can file a public prosecution based on their authority, and all child welfare organizations can report to the prosecutor and request sanctions. In certain circumstances, if there is no one to make a complaint, the prosecutor can designate a person to make a complaint on behalf of the child, according to the provisions of the Criminal Procedure Law. From this, it can be seen that those who abuse children, cripple their limbs, and profit by selling their performances are all criminals in the eyes of the law. Not only can the prosecutor file a public prosecution, but all child welfare organizations can also report to the prosecutor and request legal action. Will they now wake up, repent, and correct their mistakes?

Increase in Capital 187

The company's original capital was four million yuan, but under the 1933 asset and liability items, it reached more than eight million nine hundred thousand yuan, including more than six million two hundred thousand yuan in fixed assets, which exceeded the original capital. Now, due to the development of business, it is urgent to build a new plant, add boiler machinery, and expand equipment. Therefore, in March 1934, the company's shareholders' meeting resolved to increase capital by two million yuan, divided into two hundred thousand shares, still giving the old shareholders priority to subscribe. Every two old shares can be exchanged for one new share. The payment for the shares was collected in one lump sum, from July 16 to December 31, and two million yuan has been fully collected.

Construction of New Plant 188

Due to the increasing amount of power supplied by the company, the existing power plant's power generation capacity is not sufficient, and the old plant's equipment is not very economical in terms of power generation costs. It is necessary to build a new plant. The plant has now prepared a planning book and main engineering drawings, which have been submitted to the Construction Committee and the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau for review, so that construction can begin and machinery can be added.

Child Recounts Kidnapping Experience with Vivid Details 189

Case Concluded and Awaiting Judgment

Cai Xiqing, a native of Taizhou, thirty-three years old, living at Taifeng Lane in Caogadu, West Shanghai, was a foreman at the Taifeng Yarn Factory and had some savings. He married Li and had a son named Wenzhu, who is now seven years old. On December 21st of last year, Wenzhu suddenly disappeared. Cai Xiqing hired people to search everywhere, but there was no trace. Cai Xiqing, deeply attached to his son, posted notices everywhere offering a reward for finding his son. About half a month later, he received a letter stating that his son Wenzhu was now at the Jinwang Temple in Beixinjing. To get his son back, he needed to prepare one hundred yuan in cash and come to redeem him. Otherwise, he would face the consequences. The letter also specified that the person coming to negotiate must wear a blue cloth shirt and tie a white cloth strip around their waist for identification. After receiving the letter, Cai reported it to the responsible police station, which immediately ordered detectives in disguise to go to the location. The kidnappers Gao Lanting, Wang Jiugao, and Chen Guangle were arrested one after another, and the kidnapped child Cai Wenzhu was rescued. They were all taken to the General Bureau and transferred to the local court, where Prosecutor Kong Xianglin interrogated them and prosecuted them for kidnapping and extortion. Yesterday morning, Judge Chen Kangsun specially opened the fifth court for the trial. First, Cai Xiqing recounted the events and requested a heavy sentence. Next, the child Cai Wenzhu, seven years old, testified that Gao Lanting had tricked him and taken him to the second floor of a tailor shop (Chen Guangle's house), where he was not allowed to go downstairs. The child's account was vivid and detailed. The judge then ordered the imprisoned Gao Lanting and others to be brought to the court. Gao testified that he made a living pulling a rickshaw. On December 21st of last year, a friend named Liu Xiguan led a child past his house. He asked him where he was going, and Liu replied that he was going to Longmen Road. He thought that Liu and Cai Xiqing were cousins, so he did not suspect anything. It was not until the next day, when he saw Cai Xiqing posting notices with a reward, that he realized Liu Xiguan had kidnapped Cai Xiqing's son Wenzhu. He said he had been wrongly arrested and asked for mercy. When asked if he had written the letter, he replied that he was illiterate and could not have written the letter. Next, Wang Jiugao, thirty-nine years old, a native of Dongtai, testified that he worked in a yarn factory and lived in Caogadu. When asked what he was doing in Beixinjing, he replied that his cousin lived there and wanted to return to his hometown, so he wanted to entrust him to take ten yuan to his parents for household expenses. When asked if he could write, he replied that he could not. When asked about the child's testimony that he was present, he replied that it was a wrongful accusation. When asked how the child was rescued, he replied that he did not know. Finally, Chen Guangle, thirty years old, a native of Taizhou and a tailor, testified that Cai Xiqing's son Wenzhu had stayed at his house. He said that he went to the Zhang Mansion on Avenue Edward VII to make clothes that day. When he returned in the evening, his wife told him that a friend of hers had brought a child from their hometown to Shanghai to look for his wife, so she had temporarily lodged the child at their house. He thought it was a matter of friendship and did not expect this incident. When asked how old the child was, he replied five or six years old. When asked if he knew Wang Jiugao, he replied that he did not know him. He said he had been a neighbor of Gao Lanting eight years ago, but they had not been in contact recently. At this point, the detective Zhong Xuehuan, who solved the case, testified in court, recounting the process of solving the case. After hearing the testimony, the judge asked Prosecutor Kong to make a statement, followed by the appointed defense attorney Ji Deng Gu Qi to defend the three defendants at length. The judge, believing that the case was clear, declared it closed and scheduled the verdict for 10 AM on the 15th of this month. The three defendants were returned to custody to await the decision.

Continued Hearing of the Jiande Bank Case 198

Chai Chuangui bears heavier responsibility, posts 10,000 yuan bail.

Directors shirk responsibility, unwilling to bear it.

Following the collapse of Jiande Bank, its General Manager Chai Chuangui and all directors and supervisors, a dozen or so people, were criminally prosecuted by creditor Wei Haijiang and others at the First Special District District Court for crimes of fraud, embezzlement, breach of trust, and malpractice. After repeated summonses, as previously reported in this newspaper, yesterday afternoon Judge Liu Yugui continued the hearing. Only six defendants, including Chai Chuangui, appeared, each accompanied by defense lawyers. The other six, Ou Jiancheng, Chen Fuyi, Zheng Huaigu, Chen Xifu, Tu Kaizheng, and Chai Yousheng, were either with unknown addresses, had left Shanghai, or claimed illness, and did not appear in court. First, the lawyers representing plaintiffs Wei Haijiang and Wang Ruyao, Chen Tingrui successively stated how the defendants, including Chai Chuangui, used the lure of hiring them as deputy managers or assistants to fraudulently obtain funds from various individuals for shares and mortgage deeds. Judge Liu then interrogated each of the defendants who appeared in court one by one. Chai Chuangui stated that Jiande Bank was founded in July of the seventeenth year (of the Republic), and he served as director and general manager. In the same year, it was registered with the ministry, and it was not until the twenty-second year that it was approved by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, with a fixed capital of one million yuan and a paid-up capital of 500,000 yuan. The ministry commissioned verification of the capital, and it was certified by the City Chamber of Commerce. There is still a capital book available for verification. On December 8 of last year, due to a lack of cash and poor turnover, bankruptcy was declared, but assets and liabilities could still offset each other. Therefore, if the accounts are completely collected, deposits can be fully repaid. However, in this time of economic depression, collecting debts may not be easy. There are eleven directors on the board of directors. Unless for important matters, everything must be decided and implemented by the board of directors. Ordinary matters are handled by the general manager. Matters such as inviting Wei Haijiang and others to invest, hiring Wei and others as deputy managers and assistants, and mortgaging their deeds were all approved by the board of directors. However, the shares subscribed by Wei were not newly issued but transferred by the previous shareholder, surnamed Zhao, and Taiji, etc. Chai also denied Wei Haijiang's previous court statement that the bank's capital was only about 200,000 yuan. Judge Liu believed that Chai Chuangui bore heavier responsibility in this case and immediately ordered him to post 10,000 yuan in cash or shop as bail. He then instructed the police to take Chai to the bail office to complete the bail procedures to avoid being too late. Next, the defendants Yan Ziyu, Xie Keming, Ma Suizhi, and Li Jingwei, each gave statements. Yan claimed that he was elected as a director but never took office, so he was unaware of all the actions. He paid 2,000 yuan for his shares. Xie claimed that he subscribed for 25 shares, paying 2,500 yuan. Although he was elected as a director, he resigned last October, so he was unaware of the hiring of Wei and others as deputy managers and the mortgaging of deeds. Ma claimed that he always came to Shanghai from Suzhou to attend board meetings, but the investment of Wei and others and the mortgage of deeds were never proposed by the board of directors. Li also claimed that the mortgage and other matters were not approved by the board of directors. At this time, Chai Chuangui was brought back to the court by the police. Judge Liu questioned him about the process of mortgaging the mortgage deeds of Wei Haijiang and others to the Shanghai Bank and the Four Banks Savings Society. Chai claimed that Wei and others sought ways to raise funds to maintain the bank because they saw the financial difficulties of the bank. Wei's lawyer, Lu Jia, then presented a copy of the meeting minutes of December 10 of last year, a resolution of the fifth annual shareholder meeting of December 17 of the twenty-second year (of the Republic), and a statement from the bank's accounting director. Lawyer Lu claimed that the December 10 meeting was convened to discuss the issue of resumption of business. The directors who attended the meeting first signed the meeting minutes and then began the discussion. Regarding the capital issue, Chai Chuangui personally said that only 200,000 yuan had been paid up. The bank's accounting director's statement also said that only 200,000 yuan of capital had been paid up. At the fifth annual shareholders' meeting, Chairman Xie Keming reported on the registration situation to the ministry, stating that 250,000 yuan of share capital had been paid up, which was rejected because 500,000 yuan was required for registration. Therefore, the board of directors had to find a way to raise 500,000 yuan. These three pieces of evidence are sufficient to prove that the defendants Chai Chuangui and others' statement that 500,000 yuan of capital had been paid up is unbelievable. The license issued by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce stated that half of its capital, 500,000 yuan, had been paid up, meaning that its registered capital should be one million yuan. The lawyer wanted to present more evidence, but Judge Liu, seeing that it was getting late and the case was complex and could not be completed in a hurry, ordered the hearing to be adjourned to 2:30 p.m. on February 23 and ordered Chai Chuangui to bring the meeting minutes, capital book, stock stubs, stock payment receipts, and other important documents to the court for verification next time. × × × ×

They were employed there as gatekeepers and accountants. The owner was Chen Minghua. No. 236 Guangdong Road was a warehouse. Wang Yonggui and Gao Guoqing both confessed to being workers, working there for just over a month. Judge Qian verified the confessions and ordered the defendants to be taken back into custody, rescheduling the hearing for one week later. The police requested an on-site inspection, but the inspection was deemed unnecessary. All explosive materials were permitted to be destroyed by the police first, with a detailed list reported. Special Article

Two Lines on Japan by Lin Bosheng 203

...After Reading Xu Daolin's "A Review of Sino-Japanese Relations"...

I.

Generally, Chinese people inevitably have two habits regarding the Sino-Japanese issue: one is arrogance, and the other is depression. This is the case among the people, and it is also the case in the government. This is the greatest psychological danger building of today's nation and should be corrected.

Those who commit the first habit clearly know that their strength is insufficient, but they refuse to admit it, only spouting high-sounding words. This approach is not only deceiving others but also deceiving oneself. It must be understood that the Sino-Japanese dispute, with its unresolved grievances, has lasted a full forty years, counting only from the Sino-Japanese War. Even from the September 18th Incident to the present, it has been four years. This situation cannot be resolved by a few empty slogans. Without fundamental planning, grand words are merely pleasant to hear but utterly useless. Moreover, the five-minute enthusiasm vanishes like melting ice and snow. Once the event passes and the situation changes, everything is forgotten, and the air of vanity quickly diminishes! As for those who act impulsively, using foreign affairs as a tool for political struggle, they disregard national difficulties and are beyond consideration.

Those who commit the second habit are just the opposite. They know that military strength is inferior, international standing is inferior, political strength is inferior, and economic strength is inferior. Driven by foreign troubles and weighed down by internal worries, they find it impossible to fight and unable to defend. Exhausted and stumbling, their spirits are withered, and their wills are despondent. They are bewildered and lost, like a lone boat adrift in a dead-end harbor, resigned to fate and letting things drift, never thinking of how to extricate themselves. When discussing Japan, they either weep bitterly and dare not speak, or swallow their anger and are unwilling to speak. The worst of them hold their heads and protect their necks, as if awaiting capture and slaughter, closing their eyes and shaking their heads, like submissive subjects. Although they are not yet dead, their spirits are dead. Although the nation is not yet destroyed, the image of national ruin is deeply ingrained in their hearts. What could be more dangerous and painful than this situation!

After reading Xu Daolin's article "Enemy or Friend?", I most admire that he did not commit these two errors. He frankly pointed out the mistakes on the Chinese side and the mistakes on the Japanese side, and he stated that "the Japanese will ultimately not be our enemies, and we Chinese must ultimately have the necessity of joining hands with Japan," further proposing the path that the two countries should take.

I believe that today, people from both China and Japan should have the same attitude as Mr. Xu, not driven by circumstances, not blinded by emotions, and sincerely, calmly, and rationally seek a fundamental solution to the Sino-Japanese problem. I hope that Mr. Xu's writing can spark a public discussion among Chinese people regarding the Sino-Japanese issue and further attract the attention of the Japanese, prompting them to awaken.

I would like to discuss with Mr. Xu what I personally feel and use it to seek correction from my fellow countrymen.

II.

Mr. Xu's proposed solution to break the Sino-Japanese deadlock involves three points:

(1) On the Chinese side, "As long as Japan has the sincerity to seek a solution, China only needs to demand the abandonment of territorial aggression and the return of the four northeastern provinces. Other methods do not need to be rigidly adhered to. Past pending issues should be resolved with sincerity for mutual benefit, clearing the obstacles to diplomatic relations."

(2) On the Japanese side, "It should earnestly express its sincerity in the statement 'preserving China's unity' and 'not obstructing China's independence or interests and having no intention of harming them' (as stated in the Japanese Foreign Ministry's declaration and Hirota's remarks), resolutely return the four northeastern provinces, making them belong to China's territory, and at the same time resolve the pending issues between the two countries."

(3) "The initiative to break the Sino-Japanese deadlock naturally lies with Japan." Therefore, "This negotiation should naturally be initiated by Japan, but it is acceptable for the two countries to negotiate directly. After reaching an agreement, China will report to the League of Nations..."

How to propose, how to negotiate, and how to report are matters to be discussed after the deadlock is broken, so they will not be addressed for now. The most important thing in Mr. Xu's proposed solution is a prerequisite issue, which I believe needs to be discussed. If this issue is not resolved, then the so-called solution remains unresolved, and the so-called path remains impassable.

According to Mr. Xu's intention, it seems that regarding the responsibility for being enemies or friends between China and Japan, China accounts for 40% and Japan accounts for 60%. In that case, assuming China is willing to be friends with Japan, the extent to which it can be decided is only 40%. If Japan is determined not to be friends with China, the extent to which it can be rejected is 60%. What should be done in this case?

Mr. Xu said: "The one who tied the bell must untie it." The tying and untying of the bell naturally rests entirely with Japan. How should it be untied? Mr. Xu also said: "Japan should take the lead in proposing the return of the four northeastern provinces."

What if Japan does not return the four northeastern provinces? Does Japan's failure to return the four northeastern provinces mean that China will become an enemy of Japan? Before today, Japan has not returned the four northeastern provinces. Should China be an "enemy or friend" to Japan? If Japan does not return the four northeastern provinces after today, should China be an "enemy or friend" to Japan?

If Japan is willing to return the four northeastern provinces voluntarily, that would naturally be the best outcome. But is Japan willing to do so? There are two clear facts before us:

First, Japan's attitude towards the four northeastern provinces is at best to have us recognize Manchukuo, progressing from de facto recognition to formal recognition. From the occupation of the Northeast on September 18th of the 20th year to the League of Nations' resolution not to recognize Manchukuo in the 22nd year, Japan's efforts were aimed at making us recognize Manchukuo. After the League of Nations' resolution, it knew that recognizing Manchukuo was hopeless, so it withdrew from the League of Nations to invalidate the resolution while setting traps in all negotiations, wanting us to fall into the net and make suspicions of de facto recognition of Manchukuo. Later, seeing that the Chinese authorities would not be fooled and even this de facto recognition could not be achieved, it became even more stubborn, simply breaking free from all constraints and tearing up all treaties. The Nine-Power Treaty was abandoned, and the naval treaty was also abolished. Many people ridiculed Japan, saying it was isolating itself. Japan was indeed isolated, but what about China? Since September 18th, we have been hoping for help from other countries, but where are the other countries? We have been hoping for sanctions from the League of Nations, but what sanctions have been imposed? At the very least, the Nine-Power Treaty had some responsibility and effect in safeguarding peace in the Far East, but now even that hope is dashed. Sun Tzu said: "The best policy is to attack the enemy's plans; the next best is to attack his alliances." China is precisely in this situation today. If we say that Japan has isolated itself, the fact is that China is being trapped in isolation. The disparity between an isolated, weak nation and an isolated, strong nation is truly incomparable.

Second, Japan's consistent attitude is to take an inch and then take a mile, with no end in sight. After the Sino-Japanese War, it demanded Taiwan and the Penghu Islands. The Chinese who clung to life thought they could live in peace. After the Russo-Japanese War, it demanded Korea. The Chinese who clung to life thought they could live in peace this time. After the September 18th Incident, it demanded the Northeast, then Rehe. Who knows where it will demand next! It must be understood that occupying the Northeast is merely "a stepping stone for Japan to advance into the mainland," merely a "starting point" for its mainland policy. The ultimate interests of this "advancing into the mainland" for Japan are not discussed here, but until the Japanese awaken, they will definitely use all their strength to implement the mainland policy that they have been pursuing for fifty or sixty years. The Japanese often say: "The mainland is the true mission of the Yamato race," "How can the Yamato race live femininely on a few islands with extremely small area and extremely poor resources?" According to their long-planned plans, they will also relocate the capital with the development of national power, from Tokyo to the southern tip of Korea, from the southern tip of Korea to the banks of the Daedong River, from the banks of the Daedong River to deep into Manchuria and Mongolia. They also want to "take mainland China, Manchuria, Mongolia, and Siberia as the background, embracing the Sea of Japan and the China Sea on the left and right" to grasp the commercial rights of East Asia. They also want to monopolize East Asian industry, from Kyushu (Chikuho coal mining area), the mainland (Tokiwa coal mining area), Korea, Manchuria and Mongolia, and North China. What can we do about it?

The above points, one is Japan's fundamental national policy, and the other is Japan's attitude towards the four northeastern provinces. From the latter, it is still unknown how many opportunities for survival China will have in the future, let alone the Northeast! From the former, even if we don't ask about the future and only care about the present, it is a big question whether Japan is willing to return the four northeastern provinces. Some people believe that the attitudes of the various Japanese parties towards the occupation of the four northeastern provinces are inconsistent. This is true. Before Japan occupied the four northeastern provinces, the opinions of the various Japanese parties differed to some extent. But after they had already seized it, knowing how easy it was, how could they easily give it up? Regarding how to govern Manchukuo and how to annex Manchukuo, although there are differences in the importance and urgency of the methods, they are united as a nation in maintaining their so-called "rights and interests obtained by the blood and bones of the nation." We can say that, given the current situation in Japan, it is futile to hope that any party will be willing to give up the four northeastern provinces. In times of famine and disaster, why dream of eating meat porridge!

Or, we can say, "The Japanese are an Eastern nation and should understand Eastern psychology. The characteristics of Eastern people, especially the Chinese, are that they value emotions, integrity, etiquette, and morality." "To thoroughly renew Sino-Japanese relations, we should abandon force and focus on cultural cooperation, abandon territorial aggression and replace it with mutually beneficial economic cooperation, and abandon attempts at political control and combine with morality and emotion." However, the Japanese have said these words too many times. Aren't the Japanese currently blaming China for being too immoral and too unemotional? Aren't the Japanese talking about Sino-Japanese cultural cooperation and Sino-Japanese economic cooperation all the time? Why is it that these words have not been realized until now? Because the crux of the matter has not been removed and the separation still exists. These words have an effect on people, but they are useless to us. And to remove this crux and break this separation requires endless effort. It cannot be achieved by a few words of morality, emotion, and sweet talk.

We can also say that returning the four northeastern provinces is not without a price. Resolving pending issues is a valuable exchange condition. At this point, I cannot help but recall the situation before and after the September 18th Incident. Before the September 18th Incident, the Japanese demanded the resolution of pending issues. We acted impulsively and neglected the matter, leading to a great mistake, which cannot be denied. But is it still possible to go back to the situation before the September 18th Incident? After the September 18th Incident, we also talked about restoring the original state and starting negotiations, but what was the effect? Wasn't it just one day after another, with the original state never being restored, but negotiations had to proceed?

The so-called first returning the Northeast and then negotiating pending issues, what can we do if Japan does not return the Northeast? Not only that, but even if the Northeast is not returned, and the pending issues are to be negotiated, what can we do then?

Not only that, but even if we go a step further, Japan is willing to consider the Northeast issue, and the so-called negotiating pending issues, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' pocket will inevitably contain the so-called Twenty-One Demands, the so-called Sino-Japanese Treaty, and the so-called Sino-"Manchu" Japanese Defense Alliance. What can we do then? "Enemy or friend?" We are still walking a circular path with no beginning and no end. If we cannot jump out of this circular path, the deadlock between China and Japan will never be broken. (To be continued)

Shanghai Basketball Association A-A Division Final: Pirates Defeat McLins by One Point 204

Result: 33 to 32 points

The game was decided by a free throw in the final minute.

Black Hawks vs. McLins tonight at 8:30

Pirates and McLins met last night in the Shanghai Basketball Association A Division game, which was also the final of this year's championship. The two sides were evenly matched, and the game was extremely tense. In the end, each side relied on a free throw to determine the outcome. Carson of the Pirates made the shot, putting them ahead 33 to 32. McLins lost by one point due to Grosky's missed free throw. It was a matter of luck and misfortune. In addition, there were three other games. Among them, the A Division game between Jiangwan and East Asia was also very close. At the end of the game, each side had 33 points. Later, in overtime, East Asia finally won by a difference of four points, 39 to 35, which was unexpected. However, East Asia played very well yesterday, showing considerable progress compared to the past. The results of the other two B1 Division games were as follows: (1) Xia Guang defeated Moore, first half 8 to 7, total result 27 to 12. (2) Seven Team defeated Jianmei, first half 13 to 16, total result 32 to 17.

Pirates Win Against McLins 205

After the start of the game, the Pirates launched a preemptive strike. Smith and Ryan both shot and scored. McLins also scored by Locke. The two sides were in a stalemate for five minutes. The competition was extremely fierce. The Pirates were always in the lead because of their excellent coordination. Locke, McLins' only shooting expert, was closely guarded by Ryan, the Pirates' tall man, and could not display his strengths. As the fierce battle continued to the end of the first half, the Pirates took the lead with 17 to 14.

In the second half, both sides became tense, and the game became increasingly fierce, as it was related to the outcome of the championship. Carson and Squire of the Pirates performed the best, and the entire McLins team also gave their all. Unexpectedly, with only one minute left in the game, McLins tied the score at 32 to 32. At that time, Carson got a free throw and scored another point. Unexpectedly, with seven seconds left, Grosky of McLins also got a free throw opportunity, but unfortunately missed the shot, losing by one point. It was a pity.

City Education Bureau to Hold City-Wide Elementary School Shuttlecock Kicking Competition 209

Scheduled to be held in districts on the 23rd of this month.

Kicking methods are divided into single kick, plate kick, and cross kick, three types.

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order yesterday to all municipal and private registered elementary schools in the city, stating that shuttlecock is a good tool for children in our country to engage in healthy exercise. Previously, the Sports Committee of the Ministry of Education had sent a letter to the bureau requesting that a public shuttlecock kicking competition be held. Now that the spring semester has begun, shuttlecock can be used to guide children's sports. The bureau has decided to hold a city-wide elementary school shuttlecock kicking competition starting at 9:00 AM on February 23rd to promote it. All competition methods have been formulated, and a copy of the methods is attached, ordering all school principals to comply and not violate this order. The competition methods are recorded as follows:

(1) Time: The bureau has decided to hold a city-wide elementary school shuttlecock kicking competition in districts starting at 9:30 AM on February 23rd to promote the use of shuttlecock exercise.

(2) Location: Each district's municipal and private registered elementary schools should send representatives to the following designated locations to participate in the competition ten minutes before the start of the competition:

South Shanghai District: Wuben Attached Elementary School; Zhabei District: Shuji Elementary School

Yinxiang District: Yinxi Elementary School; Yinhang District: Yinhang Elementary School

Wusong District: Wusong Elementary School; Jiangwan District: Qiujiang Elementary School

Pengpu District: Pengpu Elementary School; Zhenru District: Zhenru Elementary School

Pusong District: Shicun Elementary School; Fahua District: Honglu Elementary School

Caojing District: Qiuzhi Elementary School; Yangsi District: Yangsi Elementary School

Tangqiao District: Tangpan Elementary School; Yangjing District: Zhenxiu Elementary School

Luhang District: Sanxiu Experimental Elementary School; Gaohang District: Peiying Elementary School

Gaoqiao District: Gaoqiao Elementary School

(Note): It is also stipulated that the Municipal He'an Elementary School will be the competition location for representatives of private registered elementary schools in the special district.

(3) Divisions: The shuttlecock competition is divided into three groups: senior, intermediate, and junior grades. Each group will have two representatives selected by each school to attend and participate in the competition.

(4) Kicking Methods: The kicking methods for each group are stipulated as follows: junior grades will perform single kicks, intermediate grades will perform plate kicks, and senior grades will perform cross kicks.

(Note): A single kick means using the inner ankle of the right or left foot to kick the shuttlecock once, which is one single kick. A plate kick means kicking with both feet crossed, one foot on top and one foot below, using the inner ankle of the left or right foot that is behind to kick the shuttlecock once. A cross kick means...

(5) Judging: The bureau will assign judges to attend and judge. The judging standards are set as follows: (1) Posture accounts for 30 percent, (2) Shuttlecock production accounts for 10 percent, (3) Number of kicks accounts for 60 percent.

(6) Registration: Each school should submit a table of the names, genders, grades, and ages of each school's representatives participating in the competition to the bureau before February 22nd.

(7) Preliminary Round: Each school should hold its own shuttlecock preliminary round for each group before submitting the representatives. The preliminary round judges will be school faculty and staff.

(8) Performance: The competition is only divided into three types: single kick, plate kick, and cross kick. Each school may temporarily add a group shuttlecock kicking activity to show the spirit of cooperation or mutual assistance, which will not be counted as competition results. However, the number of people in the group and the time required should be reported to the bureau before February 12th.

(9) Awards: The top three players with the most points in each group in each district will not only have their skills praised in the Children's Morning News, but will also be awarded prizes by the bureau.

(10) Clothing: Representatives from each school participating in the competition should wear uniforms. Those who do not have uniforms should wear domestically produced short clothes.

(11) Shuttlecocks: All shuttlecocks must be self-provided.

(12) Implementation: These measures will be implemented after being announced by the bureau.

Educational News

Zhejiang Education Department Promulgates Standards for County and City Mayors to Handle Educational Administration Assessments 216

And Six Articles of Reward and Punishment Measures

(Shanghai News Agency Hangzhou Quick News) The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education believes that county and city mayors are responsible for promoting local education. Their achievements in handling educational administration should be based on specific methods, implementing assessments, and rewarding or punishing them accordingly. Therefore, it has drafted six articles of the Zhejiang Province County Mayor and City Mayor Interim Assessment Standards and Reward and Punishment Measures for Handling Educational Administration. It has been submitted to the Zhejiang Provincial Government for approval in conjunction with the Department of Civil Affairs and transferred to the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior for record filing and implementation. The methods are recorded as follows:

Zhejiang Province County Mayor and City Mayor Interim Assessment Standards and Reward and Punishment Measures for Handling Educational Administration. Article 1: These measures are formulated in accordance with Article 13 of the County Mayor and City Mayor Interim Assessment Regulations for Handling Educational Administration. Article 2: The assessment standards of these measures are in accordance with Article 6 of the Regulations, respectively, as follows: (1) Achievements in planning, organizing, and guaranteeing educational funding: A. Those who increase educational funding; B. Those who make efforts to supervise and collect various educational surcharges and taxes and issue them on schedule; C. Those who are resourceful in adjusting when county and district educational funding is insufficient; D. Those who have clear educational funds; E. Those who have organized the rental income of school land and increased income; F. Those who have achieved significant results in organizing county and district educational property; G. Those who effectively protect educational property; (2) Achievements in handling compulsory education: A. Those who implement compulsory education plans and can proceed step by step; B. Those who have achieved significant results in planning and establishing township primary schools; C. Those who make efforts to encourage people to run schools and children to attend school; D. Those who have investigated the number of school-age children clearly and accurately; E. Those who make efforts to promote short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes; (3) Achievements in handling social education: A. Those who implement popular education and have a complete plan that can proceed step by step; B. Those who have achieved significant results in planning and establishing township popular schools; C. Those who supervise and promote the effective cooperation of construction agencies, autonomous agencies, and popular education agencies and have achieved significant results; D. Those who supervise schools to also handle popular education and have achieved significant results; E. Those who make efforts to encourage the public to run schools and attend school; Those who have investigated the number of unemployed people clearly and accurately; (4) Increase or decrease in the number of schools and students: A. Those whose number of elementary schools and students increases year by year; B. Those whose number of popular schools and students increases year by year; C. Those whose number of various vocational schools or vocational supplementary classes, class numbers, and students increases year by year; D. Those whose number of other necessary various schools and students increases year by year; (5) The quality of school content: A. More than one-quarter of the elementary schools in the county and city have excellent content; B. More than one-tenth of the popular schools in the county and city meet the standards of excellent popular schools; C. Various vocational schools or vocational supplementary schools can effectively contact various agricultural, industrial, and commercial groups; D. Other various schools that are run in accordance with regulations and have achieved effective results; (6) Others A. Those who make efforts to follow laws and regulations; B. Those who have practical plans to improve education throughout the county; C. Those who supervise and guide subordinate agencies in handling education effectively; D. Those who report work accurately and quickly. Article 3: County mayors who have any of the facts listed in the preceding article shall be rewarded, and those who violate them shall be disciplined. Article 4: The rewards or punishments in these measures shall be handled separately in accordance with Articles 4 and 5 of the Regulations and in accordance with the facts listed in Article 2 of these measures, taking into account the severity of the circumstances. Article 5: The procedure for rewarding or punishing the assessment of county mayors shall be in accordance with Articles 3 and 7 to 12 of the Regulations. Article 6: These measures shall be implemented after being submitted to the Provincial Government for approval and transferred to the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior for record filing.

(Nanjing, 9th) The Anhui Provincial Government requested that the government subsidize 250,000 yuan annually for educational funding.
