Cooperation Methods Between the National Academic Work Advisory Office and Various International Organizations 218

The memorandum on the cooperation methods between the National Academic Work Advisory Office of China and various international and national organizations has been published in the newspapers. Now, the cooperation methods between the National Academic Work Advisory Office and various international organizations are recorded as follows:

(A) "International Labor Office" The International Labor Office assists the advisory office in providing students under its supervision with the convenience of obtaining specialized knowledge and internships in the country of residence or other countries (attending specialized research institutes, interning in various administrative agencies and enterprises) so that they can be competent in their chosen profession. When the National Academic Work Advisory Office is first established, it seems necessary to hire an advisor familiar with the methods of introducing academic staff from various countries. The term of office is temporarily set at three months. This advisor can be entrusted to the International Labor Office to hire. (B) "International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation" The International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation, at its meeting on July 20, 1934, decided to fully assist the National Academic Work Advisory Office decided by the Chinese government to be established in Nanjing and the West to facilitate the vocational training of Chinese students studying in Europe and the United States to meet the needs of China's current economic construction. The committee decided to organize a small committee with Mr. Hass 郎 Zhiwen, Molede, Pietra Lomach, Shaw Tehui, and Chinese Yuan Tongli as members, whose task is to draft various suggestions and propose methods and nature of various international and national institutions to assist the Chinese advisory office. "The Chinese Academic Work Advisory Office cooperates with an international organization without political or religious nature, such as the International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation, which can dispel the concerns of certain Chinese student groups and arouse the interest of national organizations and governments." The International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation can introduce various organizations (such as universities, schools, Chinese-European university groups, Chinese and foreign associations, etc.) and governments and administrative agencies of various countries to the Chinese Academic Work Advisory Office. Before the establishment of the Chinese Academic Work Advisory Office, the International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation will contact the Chinese and foreign university committees in Europe and the United States. The institute will inform the committees of the plan to establish the advisory office and inquire whether they are willing to actively cooperate with the Western offices of the advisory office. The nature of the assistance given by the Chinese and foreign committees to the Chinese advisory office will be clearly stated later. Regarding this point, the Institute for Cultural Cooperation will also ask the committees to express their opinions. China also does not want the advisory office to hinder the undertakings that the committees have already carried out for Chinese students. The advisory office only asks the committees to also assume the responsibility of supervising students. In places where the permanent representative of China is stationed in the Geneva office, the representative should cooperate closely and liaise with the committee. "The International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation has good contacts with the university offices of various countries, the educational information centers of various countries, the educational administrations of various countries, and the famous figures and academic groups in the academic circles of various countries. If the Chinese Advisory Office needs information and assistance that it cannot obtain by itself, the International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation can provide it in the shortest time."

(C) "International Student Association" Many international student associations have been in contact with Chinese students. The Christian Student Association Federation and the International University Mutual Aid Association have branches in China. The former especially strives to attract Chinese students. In some countries, such as the United States, the organization of Chinese student associations is organized in accordance with the regulations of the International Federation. The International University Mutual Aid Association also convened a conference in Cambridge in 1933 to study and improve the living conditions of Chinese students in Europe. The association cooperates with the International Student Association Federation and the Chinese and foreign committees to organize institutions for receiving Eastern students in various important ports in Europe. Chinese students are, of course, also among the recipients. The Roman Peace Association also does not ignore Chinese students studying in the West. The above associations are very beneficial, especially during the summer, they can introduce cheap summer resorts, organize travel, etc. If a branch of the International Student Association can be organized in China, cooperation with the association will be more convenient.

(D) "Methods of Cooperation with National Organizations in Various Countries" Before the meeting of the Chinese Subcommittee (ie, the International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation organized for the Chinese Academic Work Advisory Office), the following national organizations should be consulted, and if necessary, they should be invited to attend the meeting (including the university committees of Belgium, the United States, France, Britain, and Germany, or the presidents or secretaries-general of advanced research institutes, and the Sino-French Friendship Association, etc.). The International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation should, within the above scope, ask them to assist the Geneva and New York offices of the advisory office, or in an indirect way, that is, to cooperate closely with the permanent representatives of each office stationed there. If there is no such representative, they should cooperate directly with each office. This kind of national organization has the following benefits for Chinese students: (1) It can instruct Chinese students to find accommodation, or provide reduced-price transportation tickets, scholarships, honorary loans, or relief funds for boarding in families, so that Chinese students do not feel difficult in their lives. (2) Find ways to make Chinese students interact with families in their place of residence. (3) Organize language tutoring classes and lectures on common sense. (4) Guide Chinese students' studies, provide information on teaching and research institutions, admission requirements, qualifications, examinations, and special research work. Chinese students' advisors should be people who have sufficient knowledge of Chinese life. (5) Introduce Chinese students to internships in various countries' administrative agencies, factories, and other organizations. (6) Introduce Chinese students to professors and enable them to enter research laboratories to engage in research. (7) Organize Chinese students' holiday life, introduce them to reside in foreign families, open summer special classes, organize academic trips, introduce them to holiday camping youth hostels, etc. (8) Communicate with the Chinese Academic Work Advisory Office.

Cai Yuanpei and others were elected as the presidium.

Discussed the issue of youth vocational training.

The Chinese Vocational Education Society held the tenth expert meeting at the Gaoqiao Seaside Hotel yesterday, starting at 9:00 AM. The society's affairs were reported in the morning, and proposals were discussed in the afternoon. The details are recorded as follows:

Experts in Attendance 225

Including Cai Yuanpei, Zhuang Zexuan, Yu Qingtang, Ou Yuanhuai, Chen Qingshi, Liu Zhanen, Chen Lijiang, Zhang Yousan, Huang Renzhi, Chen Jicheng, Jiang Wenyu, Yang Weiyu, Yao Huiquan, Li Gongpu, Yang Chonggao, Shi Yangyong, Liang Zhongyuan, Feng Maiying, Zhao Aifang, Jia Foru, Wang Kuisheng, Zhou Jiaoqing, Pan Gongzhan, Jiang Jianbai, He Qingru, Lu Shuyang, and more than thirty others.

Meeting Situation 226

The meeting commenced at 9:00 AM. After Mr. Jiang Wenyu delivered a speech outlining the meeting's purpose, Mr. Cai Yuanpei, Mr. Liu Zhanen, Mr. Ou Yuanhuai, and Mr. Yu Qingtang were publicly elected as members of the presidium. The China Stenography Society was responsible for all the records. Mr. Cai Yuanpei gave the opening address, Mr. Jiang Wenyu reported on the Society's activities over the past year, Mr. Jia Foru reported on the situation of the China Vocational School, Mr. Yang Chonggao reported on the general situation of the vocational guidance center's work, Mr. Lu Shu'ang reported on the facilities of the Shanghai suburban improvement area, and Mr. Zhao Aifang and Mr. Liang Zhongyuan reported on the general situation of vocational supplementary schools. The meeting adjourned for a photograph at 12:00 PM.

Expressing Opinions 227

After the various reports were completed, experts expressed their opinions. Mr. Liu Zhanen said that to remedy vocational education, (1) the Ministry of Education should be requested to issue a general order to all localities to establish genuine experimental vocational schools; (2) attention should be paid to and promoted for handicrafts education; (3) emphasis should be placed on civic education. Mr. Ou Yuanhuai said that the current call for national revival should not lean towards theory or empty talk. The specific plans of this association are quite practical, and vocational education must have the spirit of national salvation and self-strengthening. Mr. Zhuang Zexuan said that the scope of the Vocational Education Society's activities seems limited to Shanghai alone. In the future, it is hoped that in more distant places, a portion of talent, spirit, and economy can be allocated for experimentation. (4) Mr. Yu Qingtang said that it is more meaningful to conduct vocational education trials in remote areas. Mr. Chen Lijiang said that vocational training should be universal and not limited to a portion of people. Mr. Zhang Yousan said that vocational education encompasses a wide range and should be experimented with separately. Vocational education that is seemingly correct but actually wrong should be overthrown, and genuine vocational education should be promoted, and so on.

Discussion of Issues 228

The meeting continued at 2:00 PM in the afternoon, discussing specific plans for youth vocational training under the goal of national revival. After detailed discussions by various experts, the original plan was amended, passed, and implemented. Regarding Society affairs, the main points of this year's facilities and the scope of the annual meeting proposals were determined. It is said that the issue of youth vocational training will be expanded by the Society and popularized throughout the country. The meeting adjourned around 5:00 PM. In the evening, the Society hosted a banquet for the attendees.

(4) In order to improve the association's affairs, should a joint meeting of the directors and supervisors be held? It was resolved that a joint meeting of the directors and supervisors should be held every two months starting from March of this year. Who should the association send to attend? It was resolved that Standing Director Huang Zaoxiong should be sent to attend.

Setting up a Reading Club: The measures for the vocational youth reading club are as follows: (1) It will be named the Shanghai Municipal Education Association-sponsored Vocational Youth Reading Club (hereinafter referred to as the Reading Club). (2) The Reading Club will be temporarily divided into four groups: politics, economics, law, and Party principles. However, it is currently planned to first establish the politics and Party principles groups, and then gradually expand or add groups after achieving success. (3) Admitted students will be targeted at young shop assistants and apprentices in stores. (4) Each group will enroll 50 students, but classes will not be opened if there are fewer than ten students. (5) Reading time is set at 7:00 PM to 9:00 PM every Friday afternoon. (6) The study period is three months. At the end of the period, those who have not been absent from class for one-fifth of the time, or those who are rewarded by the association with equivalent certificates. (7) The reading method is that the first hour is the lecturer's systematic lecture time. In addition to the students recording and submitting it to the lecturer for review in the future, the China Stenography Society will be requested to take shorthand, and the lecture notes will be mimeographed and distributed to the students. In the future, they will be compiled into a book, which will be used as a series of books from the Municipal Education Association. The second hour is the student discussion time, and the lecturer is responsible for guidance and conclusions. (8) The reading classroom will be borrowed from the convenient Wuben Girls' High School or Minli Girls' High School. If only one class is opened, the public lecture hall of the Minjiao Hall will be borrowed. (9) All matters of the Reading Club will be presided over by one person selected from the directors of this association, or another person from the alternate directors will be selected to assist him. However, at least one director must personally attend each class to take care of it in order to show thoroughness. (10) The list of lecturers for each group will be drafted by the director of the reading club and hired by the association, but no travel expenses will be provided. (11) The start-up costs, in addition to the advertising in the Xinwenbao and Chenbao newspapers for three days when recruiting students, will cost about 30 to 40 yuan, and the cost of printing lecture notes, paper, and tea per month will be about 5 yuan. (12) The Reading Club's curriculum will be jointly formulated by the director, deputy director, and lecturers. (13) It is planned to start advertising for enrollment from March 1st and officially start classes on the 11th. (14) The Reading Club's regulations will be set separately. (15) Whether or not to continue the first phase will be decided by the association.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Pleading for the Disaster Victims 234

— Dujuan

Our fellow countrymen in the countryside, due to various ravages of natural disasters, war disasters, bandit disasters... are forced to succumb under the hand of death. Those who are fortunate enough to survive have also reached a state of absolute poverty: pawning clothes, selling utensils, selling fields and houses, and even selling their children. They seem to be sinking into the mud, but they are sinking deeper and deeper; the consumption of food, clothing, and shelter has reached a dead end, and these more than five million people are appealing in the north wind!

We who live in the cities are truly blessed. We are neither affected by war nor bandit disasters, and we spend our days in happiness, peace, and tranquility all year round. But, as if we are in heaven, if we just look up and see this serious disaster, these many haggard and starving faces, can we feel at ease?

As the saying goes, "People are not plants or trees; how can they be without feelings?" Moreover, the disaster victims are still our fellow countrymen! How should we rescue them from the fire and water? Although our strength is limited, within the possible scope, we should work hard to raise donations for them, plead for them, and also contribute to the country and the public to fulfill our responsibility as small citizens.

Poincaré 235

— Jinxi

Poincaré was the President of France. He passed away during the European War. In peacetime, the French people recognized Poincaré as a great patriot and believed that he was a great statesman who could withstand difficulties. When the European War was raging and France's situation was deteriorating, the news of Poincaré's death caused shock and grief among all the French people.

Poincaré was an extreme patriot and an unwavering believer and supporter of nationalism. In his childhood, he witnessed the tyrannical Prussian troops occupying his hometown. His young heart was filled with extreme anger and injustice. This determined his future ambition to be loyal to his country and protect its territory. Later, he wrote in his memoirs: "I cannot see what meaning there is in my existence in this world, unless there is hope for achieving the recovery of the lost land." This shows that he never forgot the cruel impression of the Prussian troops occupying his hometown in his childhood.

I don't hope that all children will become great statesmen like Poincaré in the future, but today Japan has seized our four northeastern provinces. Have children kept the painful and humiliating impression in their memories like Poincaré?

Gunpowder 237

— Yin

Children... When you set off firecrackers, do you ever think about the question, "How do firecrackers make a crackling sound?" Let me tell you, it's the sound of gunpowder exploding.

Gunpowder is made by mixing saltpeter, charcoal, and sulfur. You can make gunpowder by using 75% saltpeter, 15% charcoal powder, and 10% sulfur. Gunpowder was originally invented in our country. After the research of the Arabs, they invented the use of gunpowder in warfare. Recently, the application of gunpowder in all weapons has been increasing day by day.

When we set off firecrackers, we see a plume of black smoke with a pungent smell. This is black gunpowder. There is also a smokeless gunpowder, which was first discovered as guncotton. The manufacturing method is also very simple. Just soak the cotton in a mixture of nitric acid and sulfuric acid, let the cotton absorb as much nitric acid and sulfuric acid as possible, and after soaking, squeeze out the liquid, rinse with water until there is no sour taste, and then dry it. After drying, it can be used. However, it is very dangerous to manufacture, and cotton is easy to absorb moisture, so chemists have carefully studied and improved it to the smokeless gunpowder used today.

The manufacturing methods of smokeless gunpowder used in various countries are completely different, and the manufacturing methods are strictly kept secret. In China, no one has yet invented and manufactured smokeless gunpowder!

Gunpowder was originally prepared for use in warfare to destroy human lives and destroy buildings, which seems to be a terrible thing. However, it can blow up rocks, and it is indispensable in building roads, tunnels, and mines.

Children! When you play with something, I hope you often investigate its causes, manufacturing methods, and the raw materials used. In this way, it will be of great help to your knowledge!

"Children's Weekly" Group of Calligraphy and Painting 238

Where Is the Pig's Tail? 239

— Qiuxin

This year is the Year of the Pig, so I involuntarily came up with this game of "Where Is the Pig's Tail?" to offer to my dear compatriots as a Chinese New Year gift.

This game is very simple. When children want to play, it is best to invite a few classmates to play together, which will be more interesting. The method is simply to use a large drawing paper, draw a pig without a tail, and paste it on the wall. Then prepare a paper tail and place it nearby. Then, choose one person to come out, give him the tail with a pin inserted on it, then blindfold his eyes with a handkerchief, turn his body a few times (not too much, otherwise dizziness is inevitable), and ask him to connect the tail to the pig. When he relies on his own memory and imagination to connect, it will be laughable; because 99 out of 100 times or all are connected incorrectly. And when connecting, only one hand is allowed. Imagine that he is not allowed to use methods to find out where the pig is, and watch him connect randomly. And after one person connects, the others will follow suit one by one. Isn't that a very interesting game? Moreover, it can also be used as a competition, and whoever connects the tail can be rewarded.

(1) Welcome those who cannot read to come and see.

(2) Welcome children to come and see.

(3) Welcome those who care about education to come and see.

(4) Reading and selling newspapers, selling newspapers and reading.

Mr. Qiu Xue Performs Magic Tricks 240

— He Gongchao

Toys during the Sai holiday

Schools have winter vacation, and children will stay at home for more than ten days. If there are no toys to play with during these ten days, it will be so boring. Mr. Science is on stage today, especially to tell children how to make two kinds of toys themselves.

As soon as Mr. Science came on stage, he showed the children an olive in his hand and said:

"Our toys must be made by ourselves. Bought toys are not rare. As long as there are three of these olives, they can be made into very interesting toys." While saying this, Mr. Science took out a small knife and continued: "Use a small knife to shave off half of the olive, leaving the pit; then use two safety matchsticks, sharpen both ends of them, insert a small olive on one end, and then insert the other end on the olive that has been shaved off in the left and right directions: In this way, no matter where you put the tip of the olive pit, it will not fall down. Isn't this very fun?" Mr. Science said and did at the same time. After a while, the toy was made; when he put it on the fingertip, sure enough, no matter how he shook it, it would not fall down. "Why doesn't it fall down? This is due to the effect of the center of gravity. There are a few things we must know about the effect of the center of gravity: (1) The place where an object is placed and supports the object is called the fulcrum (for example, when an ink bottle is placed on the table, the bottom of the bottle is the fulcrum) (2) The larger the fulcrum, the less likely the object is to fall (when the ink bottle is placed on a tree, the bottom of the bottle is large, so it is not easy to fall. If you turn it upside down and the bottleneck becomes the fulcrum, it is easy to fall) (3) The lower the center of gravity, the less likely the object is to fall (when the ink bottle is placed upright, the center of gravity is in the lower part of the bottle, so it is not easy to fall. When it is turned upside down, the center of gravity moves to the upper part, so it is easy to fall) (4) If the center of gravity is outside the fulcrum, the object will definitely fall (when people stand, their feet are the fulcrum. If we lean too far forward or too far backward, then the center of gravity of the whole body will be beyond the fulcrum, and the body will fall) (5) If the center of gravity is below the fulcrum, even if the fulcrum is small, the object will not fall (the olive toy that was just made, the pit tip is the fulcrum, but its center of gravity is in the air below the fulcrum, so it will not fall.) "The tumbler is also made using the principle of the center of gravity. We can also make it ourselves during the winter vacation. First, roll thick paper into a round tube, and glue the ends with paper; the bottom must be glued into a circle, and put a round piece of lead inside the bottom; (glue it firmly with glue) Then add some images according to your own wishes; in this way, this thing will never fall, you press it down, and when you let go, it will stand up again. Because it has lead, the center of gravity of the whole is moved to a very low place, so it will not fall. | | This kind of homemade toy costs very little money, and you can learn some scientific knowledge, which is much more meaningful than buying foreign toys."

Strange Zoo 243

— Wen Yuyang

(1) The sheep is a ruminant even-toed ungulate in the vertebrate family. Its mouth and eyes are very small, its tail is also very short, it has a mild temperament, likes to live in groups, and eats grass. Its fur is soft, long, dense, and curly, which is good for making fur coats to wear, and can also be used to make wool yarn and wool fabrics. Children, now that the cold weather has arrived, what do you wear to not be afraid of the cold?

(2) The ram is a ruminant even-toed ungulate in the vertebrate family, produced in Spain and Australia. It is an improved sheep breed. It has a pair of curved horns on its head, which look like a spiral, so it is called a ram. They are strong and have fine hair, which can be used to make fur coats, wool yarn, and wool fabrics.

(3) The mouflon is a ruminant even-toed ungulate in the vertebrate family, living on the top of the Alps in Europe. Its horns are more than three feet long and look like bamboo branches. They are also very similar to goats, but they are wild and like to live in groups. They form groups of five to ten or more, led by an old ram. Children, can you be as gregarious and united as they are?

(4) The antelope is a ruminant even-toed ungulate in the vertebrate family. They often live in deep mountains in groups. It looks like a goat and a deer. Its mouth is very pointed, and its four legs are thin and long, which can run fast. It has a pair of short horns on its head and a body length of four feet. Because its horns can be used as medicinal materials and its skin can be used as leather, its skin and horns are very expensive. Children, you only need to go to a pharmacy or leather store to see the shape of their horns and skin!

Thinking of My Own Children 244

— Yi An

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (5) 245

— Xin Qing

In a short time, it flew back to the ground. It came down extremely fast. I had lost consciousness for a while. But when it rested on the ground again, I recovered and loosened the knots tied around my body. I was just in time, because its mouth was holding a large snake, and it immediately flew away.

I saw that I was now in a deep valley surrounded by mountains. These mountains were very high. The tops of the mountains were lost in the clouds. There was no way out around, all were steep rocks, so my situation was worse than before.

I walked around the area and saw that the ground was scattered with very good gems, some of which were very large. But what I saw was more than that | Because there were several large snakes in the past, I was very surprised. How big they were, the smallest could eat a large animal in one meal.

They hid in caves all day because they were very afraid of the roc, but they came out at night. I walked up and down in this valley, spending a day. I found a cave and climbed into it at night. I thought I would be safe in the cave.

The entrance of the cave was very small. After I went in, I blocked the gap with a large stone to prevent snakes from entering. I ate something, but was too scared to fall asleep; I heard the hissing of those big snakes all night.

When it was dawn, I walked out of the cave. Only because I was too afraid of snakes, I didn't think about the valuable gems scattered around my feet for a long time.

I didn't have to be afraid of snakes during the day, so I sat down to rest, but I told you earlier that I hadn't closed my eyes all night. Soon I fell asleep. I jumped awake again because I heard something falling near me, making a loud noise. At that time, I saw large pieces of meat being thrown down from the top of the mountain one after another.

Grain and Flour Prices Decline, Hope for Stability 260

Yesterday's flour market saw a fluctuating and stable trend in the morning and after-hours sessions. Despite the rise in quoted prices for imported wheat, the market sentiment remained flat after the opening. However, spot prices for imported wheat were quoted 3 to 4 cents higher than the previous day, giving a slightly positive outlook to the prices for various months. In subsequent sessions, although there were fluctuations in the current month, the bulls in the silver market continued to sell, weakening the market. Deferred months stabilized as manufacturers did not sell. Looking ahead, if demand from merchants improves, the situation may stabilize. As a result, the current month fell by 1 cent, March by 0.25 cents, April rose by 0.5 cents, May remained unchanged, June fell by 0.25 cents, and July rose by 1.25 cents.

Imported Wheat Continues to Rise, Domestic Wheat is Sluggish 261

Yesterday's wheat market remained stagnant after the opening in the morning. Prices for imported wheat were around 2.25 to 2.30 yuan in Chicago and slightly higher in Canada. Trading in various months was extremely quiet after the opening, with only a few cars of February and March wheat being traded. When the market opened in the afternoon, the market sentiment was slightly positive due to the stability in the flour market and the quote of 4.875 yuan for Australian wheat, which was 3 to 5 cents higher than the previous day. However, the future depends on whether imported wheat continues to stabilize, to avoid repeating the mistakes of previous years. As a result, the current month rose by 4 cents, March by 1 cent, and April by 2 cents. Spot wheat remained sluggish and no transactions were made due to lack of demand from mills.

The Chicago grain market is small, and many long positions have been closed. Those who previously shorted have made some covering purchases. Winter wheat lacks sufficient moisture. There have been some small new purchases in the corn market. Spot prices remain high with no signs of easing. If industrial demand improves, it should boost market sentiment.

Hsien Rice May Fluctuate Once 262

Yesterday's market conditions for foreign hsien rice were boosted by the previous day's price surge. However, after merchants from the interior purchased a batch the previous day, they were focusing on picking up and shipping the goods, and felt the prices were too high, intending to temporarily wait and see. Sellers, on the other hand, feeling that the production costs were high and demand was strong, intended to raise prices, resulting in a decline in trading volume. Red rice and brown rice, etc., which had risen excessively the previous day, fell slightly by about 1 cent, and only about 1,500 bags were traded. However, the price of foreign rice remained stable as foreign merchants were optimistic and production costs did not loosen, but trading also contracted. The entire market saw only 5,400 bags of Saigon and Siamese rice traded, as well as 200 tons of road goods. Based on yesterday's situation, the market is expected to fluctuate once more.

Stockpile of Rice in the Xinzha River Reduces 263

Since the major shutdown and business closure this spring, lasting for more than ten days, only three or four companies in the industry have made a profit, while the rest have suffered losses. Six companies are undergoing liquidation, reflecting the poor state of the economy. Last year's river mill inventory was two to three times less than the previous year. This spring's survey shows that the river mill inventory consists of a total of eighty to ninety boats, mostly white japonica rice, followed by inferior rice, with various types being scarce. The inventory in various foreign firms amounts to over 100,000 bags of white japonica, nearly 20,000 of inferior rice, and less than 5,000 bags of customer-specified rice. There are also over 200,000 bags of foreign rice. The industry will resume business on the tenth day of the new year. The market price report for today will be released.

Soybean Oil and Bean Cake Prices Rise Slightly 264

Yesterday's soybean oil and bean cake market saw a slight increase in prices across the board, primarily because the market first stabilized after the previous day's weak performance, then heard reports of rising prices in Dalian, leading to an increase in the exchange's standard prices, which boosted sentiment in the spot market. As for soybean oil, the peanut oil market remained firm, and the bean cake sales were brisk. Merchants from Xiamen and other regions were inquiring, with total trading volume for both current and forward contracts reaching 64,000 to 65,000 catties. Prices rose by 2 cents in the morning and afternoon. Soybean mills also began purchasing, with the mills buying four cars of Yingzhou soybeans at prices ranging from 3.78 to 3.875 yuan, two cars of Mengcheng soybeans at 3.67 yuan, one car of Bengbu soybeans at 3.65 yuan, and over 2,000 bags of Guide soybeans at prices ranging from 3.85 to 3.875 yuan. Merchants from Fuzhou bought over 500 bags of Guide soybeans at 3.90 yuan, merchants from Guangdong continued to buy over 800 bags of Xicheng soybeans at 4.50 yuan and 4.475 yuan. Merchants from Wenzhou and Taizhou, along with merchants from this street, bought over 900 bags of Hankou Zha beans at prices ranging from 3.775 to 3.70 yuan. The remaining transactions were sporadic. The above prices were generally firm, with the exception of Hankou beans, which were slightly softer by 2 to 3 cents.

Sugar Market, Guangdong Coarse White Sugar Slightly Rises 265

Yesterday's sugar market trend was flat. The association set the price of Guangdong coarse white sugar at 17.73 yuan, up 3 cents. Number 9 Dutch red sugar was 13.40 yuan, and Taikoo B Mark was 19 yuan, down slightly. The price of the factory's own fine white sugar also eased due to the decline in the price of coarse sugar. Zhenyu Number 1 was 17.40 yuan, Number 2 was 17.30 yuan, Number 3 was 17.15 yuan, and Number 4 was 17 yuan. Zhenji Renzi brand crystal sugar was 22 yuan, Ganzi was 21.90 yuan, and this factory's bagged crystal sugar was 21.50 yuan. Merchants from Guangdong and Chaozhou offered 400 pieces of basket-packed green sugar and 200 cases of sheet-packed green sugar, all priced at 9.60 yuan, and over 100 bags of branch-shaped red sugar at 12.20 yuan, 12 yuan, and 11.80 yuan. It is rumored that a new company is being organized with a capital of 80,000 yuan, which may materialize soon.

Few Sugar Businesses are Profitable 266

Few sugar businesses made a profit after the end of last year's season. It is reported that only five or six companies made significant profits, including Yuanhe with 30,000 yuan, Yantaiheng with 20,000 yuan, Guanghe with 17,000 yuan, Xiehe with 10,000 yuan, Yuansheng with 22,000 yuan, and Hexing with 8,000 yuan. Followed by Heyuan with 4,000 yuan, Maofeng with 5,000 yuan, Baowei with 5,000 yuan, and Shengji with 5,000 yuan. The rest were mostly break-even or loss-making. Hengxing and Maohe have closed this year, and there are still about one or two companies reorganizing. There are no reports of new companies being formed.

North-South Goods, Raw Peanuts Rise by 40-50 Cents 267

Due to the increase in spot prices in the Guangdong and Hong Kong sales regions by 50-60 cents, and low inventories in the production areas, the raw peanut market is very strong. Therefore, the Shanghai market opened with prices rising by varying amounts of 30-50 cents. The previous day, Kaifeng peanuts were offered at 8.30 yuan per 2,000 bags, cocooned peanuts at 8 yuan, Guide peanuts at 7.80 yuan, and Dangshan peanuts at 7.30 yuan. Yesterday, 200 bags of Qinhuangdao peanuts were offered at 8.50 yuan, and this street bought 100 tons of Kaishou peanuts, with merchants from Guangdong purchasing them at 8.40 yuan. Lower-grade Dangshan peanuts were also needed at over 7.00 yuan, and further developments are being watched.

The first batch of daylily was offered at over 100 bags, top-grade at 23.50 yuan, Daxing at 22 yuan, Yanghuaguo at 21.50 yuan, and township daylily at 29.50 yuan. Over 40 pieces of Sichuan fungus were offered at 104 yuan. Hankou original package fungus leaves were priced the same. Yichang fungus was at 90 yuan. The opening price of black melon seeds remained stable. Dangshan seeds and Da Jinbian seeds were both at 9 yuan, and Mingguang seeds were at 7 yuan.

Hardware, Black Iron Sheet Seems Strong but is Weak 268

The recently announced price by the Black Iron Sheet Association is estimated at 10.025 yuan per dan, while thick colored sheets are priced at 9.50 yuan, each being 50 cents to 1 yuan higher than at the end of last year. However, in the past two days, the buying side has been observing, resulting in limited transactions. Those holding inventory are showing signs of loosening due to the high prices, so the situation appears strong but is weak. It seems that the price per dan may fall by 20-30 cents. The association only issued 30-40 dan, which were all factory-related transactions. Due to the high prices, there were few bulk purchases.

A Significant Amount of Eastern Goods and Hardware is Being Procured 269

Recently, the Eastern exchange rate has weakened significantly, with 100 yuan being worth about 127 yuan. As a result, local companies have a strong interest in purchasing Eastern goods. Over the past two or three days, it has been reported that a large quantity of Eastern hardware has been transacted, including 2,000 bundles of new lead wire, 30,000 to 40,000 sheets of Eastern galvanized iron, over 1,000 bundles of garden lead wire, and a considerable amount of other copper sheets and copper wire.

Silk and Tea, Silk Market, Buyers and Sellers Are Unwilling to Compromise 270

The silk market remains dull. Although the telegrams received yesterday showed that overseas silk prices had risen compared to yesterday (the US market price today is 1.36 yuan), the exchange rate has also risen, which is still far from the Shanghai silk price. Furthermore, manufacturers remain firm in their intentions, so there are no transactions. There is also no market for domestic users.

Piece Goods and Woolen Fabrics Industry, Few Profits 271

The woolen fabrics industry in the 23rd year appeared strong but was weak, with apparent profits but many unpaid accounts. It was inevitable that payment to the firms would be difficult from time to time. Among the companies with the largest turnover in the industry throughout the year, Chunhe, Yonghua, Xinxinfenghua, Huafu, and Yikang were among the top five. Only Yikang and Lianxing had profits of over 20,000 yuan, and Yichangtai, Chunhe, Yonghua, Huafu, Xinchang, Chengda, and five others had profits of over 10,000 yuan. Xinfeng, Hefenghua, Kangda, Lunmei, Lunhong, Xiangyu, Kangan, Hejinfeng, Zhaoji, Jiufeng, Wangxingchang, Yuchangxiang, Wangshuntai, and thirteen other companies had profits of three to five thousand. Mouji, Mouda, Mouxin, Mouxing, and four or five other companies had losses. In summary, out of over forty companies in the woolen fabrics industry, in addition to the twenty mentioned above with profits and the four or five with losses, most of the other twenty companies broke even.

Sundries, Domestic Cowhide Suddenly Rises by Ten Yuan 272

Cowhide demand has mainly relied on imports from Rangoon. In recent years, due to increased tariffs, imports have decreased significantly, leading to the rise of domestically produced Qiongzhou Shajiang red leather as a substitute. Moreover, its color and luster are even better than red goods, so it is used as a substitute in various sales regions. Due to the sharp contraction of Guangdong exchange rates at the end of last year, the source of supply decreased, and the trend became tight. The opening market was enthusiastic, with the price suddenly rising by ten yuan. Shajiang red leather opened at 65 yuan, and water red leather at 45 yuan. Other white back leather and water stiff leather have not risen or fallen because they are not currently in the sales season.

First Anniversary of the Women's Garden

A Small Hope 290

— Cai Muhui

I can't remember if it was "Rebirth Fate," "Brush Generates Flowers," "Heavenly Rain of Flowers," or some other "·········." When that author was writing a certain section, she put down her pen for a long time because she had to do chores for the New Year. When she picked up her pen again, it was already after the Lantern Festival, so she inserted her own family life into the novel. In the eyes of a literary critic with strong traditional ideas, this might be said to be inconsistent with the methods of novel writing and absolutely should not have happened. But to me, who values life more than literature, it left an extremely deep impression. Now, it may have been a full twenty years since I read that novel. The story in the novel is almost completely forgotten, but the author's digression is still very vivid and clear. This is probably because women's lives have always been recorded only in abstract, commentary-style, or fictionalized essays or novels. There are very few sketches in the style of everyday talk. Although this kind of sketch is too simple in the eyes of some people, those who pay attention to real life feel that it is more valuable than any other kind of article.

This year, except for a few Sunday mornings when special events occupied my attention, I have seen almost every issue of the Women's Garden. Sometimes I see a lot of beautiful and delicious exotic flowers, which makes me reluctant to put them down. Sometimes I only see a few simple and haggard ordinary blades of grass, which also makes me watch them back and forth. I feel that my state of mind is like Tennyson's (Tennyson) appreciation of the green grass growing in the cracks of the prison wall, feeling that carefully looking at that simple blade of grass can penetrate the highest philosophy of the universe. The reason is that a real blade of grass can make people understand the truth of life better than a fake flower. A plain photo of an old friend who can resonate with one's own life is more valuable to watch carefully than a beautiful artistic photo of a peach blossom or a star. In the past year of this magazine, although I liked several kinds of magazines very much, the one I read most diligently was the Women's Garden, and it was for this reason.

However, I have further expectations for the future of the Women's Garden. First, I hope that the gardeners' characters will be more diverse and rich. In addition to exploring and recording the lives and paths of educated women, I also pay more attention to the masses of women living in factories and fields. If the people living these lives can take on the responsibility of introducing themselves, it would naturally be even more interesting. Second, I hope that the flowers in the garden will grow more freely, whether it is "A-da crying for peanut rice, A-er crying for shit, A-da's father moaning for boiled water, and A-da's mother is busy writing an article for the Women's Garden or other publications" or "Manager's tricks and Mrs. Manager's suspicions," both sides of women's lives can be written in a very real and unrestrained way. Don't be too conservative and gentlemanly. Writing articles too formally and elegantly, too like a serious matter, will lose the true flavor.

Because there are more and more publications that solve problems and pass the time for women in the knowledge class and the leisure class, those sisters who are groaning under the double burden of housework and work not only do not have the time to do the detailed work of biting words and phrases, arranging layouts, and practicing writing, but also do not have the time to sit quietly and appreciate the literary talent that is irrelevant to life!

I really admire the female writer who gave me such a real impression twenty years ago. She made me realize that even a vulgar person who has no time to appreciate flowers and the moon can write a few sentences. Otherwise, perhaps even now, I would still be superstitious that only those who live like angels, untouched by the mundane world, are worthy of playing with words.

In order to help celebrate the first anniversary of the Women's Garden, I have hastily drafted these few words in the midst of my busy schedule. Perhaps only busy people will agree with my proposition.

Women's Issues in the Past Year 291

— Bi Yao

The new calendar is now mid-February, but the old calendar is still the beginning of the new year. The old always has its ancient fragrance in people's minds, so the women's issues floating in the ancient country for a year are also settled at the end of the old calendar, according to the merchant's method. Last year had a leap fifth month. In the thirteen months of the year, the following events happened in the women's sector, neither light nor heavy:

The first blow was the "Women's National Goods Year." National affairs have been like a mess this year. From the mess, a clue to save the country was picked out, that is, women's use of national goods. However, those who spoke earnestly were ignored by those who listened; after half a year of implementation, there was a report of 600,000 in lace consumption and 850,000 in imports of powder and perfume. As a result, social figures were greatly shocked. They thought that if women were so unwilling to work hard, the only chance to save the country would be cut off. Therefore, women's strange clothes and glamorous outfits became the target of public criticism; all parts of the North and South took the ban on women's dress as their business. Beiping still believed in the old royal style, calm and generous, only prohibiting women from bare feet and bare legs. Guangdong further demonstrated the enterprising spirit of the maritime country, and went on to prohibit men and women from bathing together, even living together, eating together, and walking together. Storms and rains made a lot of noise in all directions. Then a fundamental solution was produced, returning to the source, calling them back to the family; in this way, not only would they have fewer opportunities for glamorous outfits, but also less ability to do so. Thus, the ancient doctrine of virtuous wives and good mothers was revived. Under this atmosphere, many girls' schools that used to be called for cultivating social talents were trying to run education for virtuous wives and good mothers. Although a few people were discussing "What about Nora after she leaves?", the situation clearly told us, "Call her back home!"

Everyone paid attention to the home, and the problem of family safety and social morality arose, and then there was a very long tail. From banning women's decorations, distinguishing the badges of song girls, and detaining prostitutes who solicit customers, to the solemn formulation of provisions for punishing married women for adultery by the Legislative Yuan, the highest tide was set off. At that time, many women's organizations were organized in Beijing, Shanghai and other places, striving for equal laws. In dozens of days, they ran around calling out, and finally the one-sided criminal law of punishing "married women who commit adultery with others" was revised to "those who have a spouse and commit adultery with others shall be sentenced to imprisonment for less than one year." Women, who had been silent for a long time and allowed others to slander them, won the victory in terms of regulations.

How about women who have obtained equal rights in criminal law in other aspects? Let's not talk about the common practice of selling wives and daughters in the lower classes; let's just say that in the upper classes, where there is more freedom and less shackles, two major events have occurred in the last few days of the year. One is that Ms. Wei Wenxiu, the concubine of the late President Li Yuanhong, remarried to businessman Wang Kuixuan, which aroused criticism from Li's relatives and even more condemnation from Hubei fellow villagers, and finally led to her being deported by the Qingdao government. The other is that Sha, the concubine of Lu Dipin, the former chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, who died in Beijing, fell from the building and martyred herself. Ms. Wei lived in a land of ritual and righteousness. At a time when Guangdong and southern China were holding "widows' banquets," she destroyed her chastity and remarried, which aroused public outrage (?) which is a pity; Ms. Sha lived in the last days, but she was able to die for her husband, and social figures should silently pay their respects. These two events, one humiliating and one glorious, played the finale of the Jiaxu Year of Women.

In general, the so-called women's issues in the past year are very different from those in the Northern Expedition period. At that time, women were in dire straits, and the focus of the problem was on arousing them to liberate themselves from the shackles of thought and habit; how to seize jobs and seize economic rights; how to fight against oppressors and imperialists. They looked at the old ideas, systems, powers, and everything with contempt and boldness. However, this kind of typical woman was not needed last year. The women needed last year were quiet, chaste, virtuous, dignified and docile. Their value lies not in their own abilities and contributions to society, but in the images they reflect in the eyes of the objective. Therefore, the focus is on their clothing materials, the size of their clothes, their hair, their leather shoes, their chastity, their...... If the women encouraged during the Northern Expedition are compared to lionesses, then the women required last year can be compared to sheep. The former is suitable for charging into battle in a thorny jungle, while the latter is suitable for leisurely wandering in a mulberry garden and grass path. The changes of the times are reflected in women with such differences!

The old accounts of women's issues last year are roughly concluded in this way. Are there some people who think they are satisfied, or some people who think they are disappointed?

Women's Garden First Anniversary 292

— Editor

Ordinary women are already struggling under double oppression. China is a semi-colonial country, and Chinese women are living under triple oppression! It is easy to imagine the imperfections of a garden born under such circumstances.

The garden we initially acquired was not only laden with ice and snow, but also strewn with rubble. How could we plant good seeds? Yet, we have finally bravely cultivated it for a year. Though the tender shoots growing under the flagstones are inevitably crooked and weak, we are neither pessimistic nor sentimental. We irrigate and cultivate as much as possible. After a year of arduous management, we cannot speak of achievements or harvests. However, in this stagnant atmosphere, one can hear one or two sluggish sounds of hoes, and on that desolate wasteland, it seems that some tender shoots and green leaves can already be seen. Though the sprouts are crooked, they are born deficient; but as long as they are not imbalanced or unduly ravaged later on, it is not difficult to hope that they will grow into a lush forest. With this hope, we would like to give a brief report on the work of the past year, firstly to fulfill the obligation of accounting, and secondly to review the past and look forward to the future. The following is a brief report of our work:

(1) In view of the past stagnation of the "Women's Movement," we have called for a re-stirring of the "back wave." We anticipate that the "back wave" of 1935 will be greater than last year's ripples;

(2) With the undertow of the revolutionary tide, the "Nora" who had already left are returning home one by one. When the slogan "Women are Returning Home" reached our East Asian continent, there was a great debate in our garden. The conclusion was that not only the new women of the future new China should not be kitchen maids, homebound slaves, or men's playthings, but even the women of this transitional era must strive to be "social beings."

(3) In the past year, women's clothing and grooming seem to have received special attention. However, ordinary lower-class women are merely seeking survival on the borderline between life and death, and cannot afford to talk about how to groom or dress. Their lives are perhaps not experienced or understood by ordinary people; therefore, we often use a corner of the garden to reveal sketches of their lives. It is a pity that statistics are lacking, and we are further limited by the environment, making it inconvenient to be explicit.

(4) We strive to eradicate the enslaving mold of "Three Obediences and Four Virtues" and the feudal remnants of "remaining faithful to one husband until death," and strictly prevent the tender shoots and green leaves from being needlessly damaged.

(5) The words of the great thinkers of the world are the trends and perspectives of the times. Their opinions on women's issues are precisely the reference materials for our planting. In addition, biographies of famous people can serve as our lessons. We have already published quite a few in the past, and hope to continue to do so in the future.

(6) The most important issue among women's issues is the issue of childcare. We have published a special issue on this topic. There have been many discussions on public childcare, and it is believed that nurseries are already a necessary item in modern society.

(7) We published a special issue, among which "My Ideal Future Life" was the most interesting. The results of the call for submissions showed that although there were many who were ignorant, there were also many who were clear-headed, which is quite optimistic.

(8) The movement to fight for laws started in Nanjing and continued in various places. We waved the flag to support the cause in our garden in the rear, and at the same time, we hope to use the spirit of fighting for laws to promote the fundamental oppression.

(9) Since the "May Fourth" Movement, the emergence of intellectual women on the social stage has been the most noticeable, especially the various writers and their works. Now, we are re-evaluating their works correctly, not only to give the authors 丨丨the living and the theory丨丨to self-examine, but also to benefit the readers infinitely. We still hope that various critics will contribute more articles in the future.

(10) In order to regulate the boring hard text, we try to insert some soft writing and common sense in each issue as much as possible.

The above are the points that we think are particularly worth mentioning. As for the detailed work, we can only omit it.

The past work and expectations are as mentioned above. In the future, in addition to continuing to work hard and strive to publish, we would also like to announce the work that we want to add in the near future:

(1) Restore "Reader Correspondence" to do some practical guidance work. We have also hired a lawyer as a legal consultant. Readers can write to inquire. We will try our best to reply.

(2) Introduce more beneficial books and newspapers that should be read, hoping that it will become a beacon in the garden, so as to avoid those who seek knowledge from groping in the dark.

(3) Open a special lecture on women's issues, using the most simple language to give a simple and systematic talk on women's issues. So that everyone knows why women's issues have become a problem, and the future trends.

(4) Publish more sketches of the real lives of women at home and abroad.

(5) Collect news about women's movements at home and abroad. Enrich the garden's knowledge.

In the past year, although we have asked ourselves to work bravely, we have been limited by our abilities and forced by the environment, so that it cannot become a perfect garden. We also hope that readers will work together to cultivate it, so that this small garden can become more prosperous and grow!

A Tragedy of 1934: Rural Bankruptcy and Rural Women 293

— Junhui

"Rural bankruptcy!" This is the terrible cry of grief and sorrow of the people across the country! It is also the most cruel social tragedy staged by countless peasants! The expansion and deepening of this tragedy has become a matter of life and death for the entire nation. No matter how much people like to gloss over the truth or praise the status quo, they cannot deny that this tragedy is constantly being performed all over the country! And in this shocking tragedy, rural women are the characters that occupy the main position!

This tragedy began to be played when the commodity economy of imperialism broke through the Great Wall and invaded the Chinese countryside. Up to now, the plot has become more and more tense! Therefore, the audience in the audience, of course, want to sigh, and even the writers and directors of this tragedy, also want to promote some relief, some revival! But all this is nothing more than a farce to cover up this cruel fact! But this extremely tense tragic scene cannot be eased in any way!

Especially in the past year, the bankruptcy of the rural economy, trapped by the unprecedented interaction of floods and droughts, has accelerated its breadth and depth. According to the Nanking telegram of August 21 of this newspaper, "The disaster area has spread to more than two-thirds of the country. Fourteen provinces and 343 counties have been affected by the drought, and 13 provinces have been affected by the flood. In addition, 8 provinces and 68 counties have been affected by locust plagues, and 12 provinces and 89 counties have been affected by hail and frost. The total loss is more than 1 billion yuan." Behind this alarming number, we can vaguely see the situation of countless peasants drifting and struggling under the black line of death.

Rural women, who account for half of the country's farmers, play an even more tragic program in this tragedy of drastic bankruptcy. I would like to use some of the information in the newspapers here to briefly explain the plot they have played.

The first is to go out to work as maids. The only way out for rural women in the midst of hunger and cold is to run to the city to work as female workers. However, the city's industry is affected by the recession, and workers are being laid off in batches, and even factories are closing down. Where else is there room to accommodate them? So they joined the headhunters and became the reserve army of maids.

According to the Damei Evening News of September 2, "This year, the drought in various counties of Jiangsu is very severe, so that the autumn harvest is hopeless, and farmers are panicked about food. As a result of the bankruptcy of the countryside, women from various counties have flocked to Shanghai to find jobs. They all enter the maid introduction agencies to wait for people to hire them, but only 40% of them can get jobs, and the rest are sitting idle hungry. According to detailed investigation, there are more than 500 maid introduction agencies in Shanghai. Each introduction agency has an average of 35 to 40 people who want to get a maid job. Only a very small number of people can get a job every day. Statistics show that more than 2,000 people want to find a maid job."

According to the Jiangpu Correspondence of the Ta Kung Pao on July 16, "This county has not rained since the summer, and the drought has already appeared. Women in the southwest area of the county have gone out to work as maids in succession because there is no food to eat. They leave their hometowns in groups to seek a full meal. The situation is very pitiful."

The situation of poor women working as maids in wealthy families in the countryside is even more tragic. For example, rural women in the suburbs of Xi'an, "mostly work as servants in wealthy families. The wages they receive are only 5 yuan a year, excluding the food and accommodation provided by the master. What they eat is mostly the leftovers of the master. The master eats wheat noodles, and the coolies eat mostly coarse grains. Therefore, there are two kinds of food with distinction in one family two meals a day, so their working life is no different from cattle and horses." (Hong Kong Industrial and Commercial Daily, March 14, Xi'an Special News)

The second is to become prostitutes. The fact that rural women become prostitutes is vividly described by Ji Xun:

"Whether in the countryside or in the city in northern Jiangsu, it is filled with poisonous and foul air. Open prostitutes and secret prostitutes are everywhere... Some rural women who have just been abandoned by the land take prostitution as their profession, and some take prostitution as their sideline. There are many young girls who are lonely and helpless. They are less than 14 years old. The virginity is trampled on, and they lose their health and destroy their physical development. Their lives are completely controlled by the procuress. However, most of them are sentenced to death by syphilis before they reach adulthood! Among them, there are also housewives who have to sell their chastity in exchange for family consumption because their children are crying from hunger and cold." (Zhonghua Daily, November 2-3)

The degree of proliferation of prostitutes is proportional to the degree of rural bankruptcy and recession. In October last year, the Public Concession Police Department arrested more than 1,000 secret prostitutes in one month. These are the phenomena caused by the recession and rural bankruptcy.

According to the Guangzhou 72nd Bank News (January 15 last year), "Since the silk industry has been in recession, nearly 100 silk factories in Nanshun have closed down. Tens of thousands of silk reeling women who used to rely on them for food and clothing have now become unemployed. These women mostly have bad customs and adhere to the doctrine of not returning home. They have now lost their ability to live independently, so most of them become maids. Those who do not know how to cherish themselves mostly move to quiet places in the market towns and secretly engage in ugly business."

The Shanghai Correspondence of the Nanning Republic Daily (June 14) is a poetic description of the fact that Suzhou women fall into brothels due to rural bankruptcy, that is, "Whenever the lights are first turned on, the taverns are filled with salted duck. Upstairs and downstairs, front and back, red and green. At the same time, there are also secret prostitutes running around with the old women on the road. It is said that there are about 2,000 such women in the area of Lümen (not counting the city). In the past two or three years, disasters have been frequent, and the rural economy has gone bankrupt. It is thought that more Suzhou women have been forced to jump into the fire pit because of their livelihood." The third is to be sold as slaves. In a society dominated by , the phenomenon of selling often exists. However, in the current process of cruel rural economic bankruptcy, this phenomenon is becoming more and more widespread.

According to the Xiaofeng Correspondence of the Southeast Daily (August 6), "Recently in the city, villagers often bring their children to the city to sell them, especially girls around the age of ten. They are sold to wealthy families as maids. The price is no more than 20 yuan... "

According to the Huzhou Correspondence, "In various places in western Zhejiang, the countryside is frequently going bankrupt. Who would have thought that this year's drought would cause a disaster, and the autumn harvest would be hopeless. At the same time, the price of silk has plummeted, falling directly to 13 or 4 yuan. The plight of the peasants is beyond words. Among them, the obedient ones eat wild vegetables and bark to fill their hunger, and sell their wives and children to pay off their debts. When they are forced to the point of no return, they commit suicide... "

The fourth is suicide. The tragic events of rural women "committing suicide by jumping into the river" and "hanging themselves" due to the pressure of life and lack of rice to cook are often heard in the newspapers, but due to the limited space, I cannot give examples here. Please forgive the readers.

All in all, the program played by rural women in this tragedy of rural bankruptcy is particularly tragic! Rural women account for more than 80% of the country's women, and they are all productive masses with labor capacity.

Who is the "New Woman"? 294

— Xian

After watching "New Woman"丨

Bearing the burden of life, how many leisurely days have I enjoyed? It was an accidental opportunity that squeezed me into the Jincheng Cinema to watch "New Woman" produced by Lianhua No. 2 Factory; this is considered very lucky.

I don't want to criticize the artistic value of this film here. It's just that after watching this film, I have a question: who exactly is the "New Woman"?

Under the current situation in China, a real "New Woman" cannot be produced, just as the "New Woman" cannot be performed on "New Woman". In this film: if we say that A Ying is the "New Woman," the impression she gives us is too lacking in depth and too hidden. "She" cannot be very active and prominent even on the screen, almost to the point that we don't pay attention to her.

Wei Ming is only an "incomplete," "fallen," "New Woman." She only jumped out of the tangible circle of old ethics, but finally could not jump out of the invisible iron ring of old ethics. What class of women does she represent in the identity she performs? We can see it in her vanity of hiding her background and the kind of life she lives.

Wei Ming's background is undoubtedly a young lady from a family of scholars for generations. This can be seen in the section where her sister tells her daughter the history of her struggle to leave the family in the past: and she is also an educated intellectual woman. Such women are too deeply poisoned by feudal ideas to jump out of that class; because of their status, she cannot dress simply and endure hardship like A Ying. If Wei Ming's position were given to A Ying, I believe A Ying would definitely be able to handle it with ease, without any problems. 丨Not only could the child be saved, but she would not die, and she would have already avenged the various insults she suffered from society.

Wei Ming attaches so much importance to chastity, which is of course a characteristic of the personality of such women. She would rather watch a smart and lively beloved daughter die than sacrifice her chastity. Her selfishness has reached this point. As for "enduring humiliation and bearing heavy burdens," selling chastity and saving other people's lives, think about it: which thing is more able to show the nobility and greatness of a woman's personality?

I don't want to encourage new women not to have chastity and deliberately destroy their bodies for revenge. However, under the current situation, the misfortune of women is unavoidable; those who are in the situation, weigh the pros and cons: if they have to sacrifice, why should we care about chastity and hurt the overall situation?

Ruan Lingyu's Wei Ming in "New Woman" is a fallen woman; lacking the "bravery," "sacrifice," "simplicity," and "endurance" of the "new spirit" and "new morality" of the "New Woman." Our real "New Woman" A Ying only occupies an unimportant position here and has not been revealed directly. 丨This is what the female group who have watched "New Woman" should recognize clearly.
