Amateur Chat

Talking About Self-Study 295

— Li Anfu

In the current society, there are many people who are engaged in occupations but feel that their knowledge is not enough. Everyone is saying this: "It's a pity that I am a poor person and I read a few years less." Or: "Why didn't my father let me read a few years more?" When we first hear this kind of words, we may sympathize with him and feel sorry for the environment he encountered. However, if we go through a thorough consideration, we can find that his saying this is just moving words on the mouth; in fact, he does not really need to want to study, or at least he still thinks that studying and seeking knowledge is a difficult thing. This is what we dare to assert.

If we open any book recording the success of mankind, whether Chinese or foreign, ancient or modern, or any kind of subject, most of them are people who self-studied or even studied hard in their early years, but they are shining brightly and are worshiped by later generations. Undoubtedly, moving and dazzling titles and qualifications may not be obtained without money; however, outside the door of learning, there is no sign saying "No Entry for Idlers". It is always smelling the door and welcoming anyone to walk into this door, and it will never discriminate against you because of your poverty; its tolerance may be more practical and reliable than the gifts of Bodhisattva or God. From this, it can be seen that those who sigh that they have no books to read are not being rejected by books, but they do not want to read them. That is to say, in their lives, there is not no way to read books, but they have a way and they just stand by the road and sigh and do not want to walk up.

However, is self-study absolutely unconditional? With what conditions can one embark on this path of self-study? Yes, this condition is not only the condition for self-study, but also the secret to the success of all kinds of careers in life; needless to say, that is concentration and perseverance. In China, there are almost countless maxims about this kind of thing and the history of successful people; even in the words and deeds of successful people in foreign countries, there are also many that can be used as mottoes for our self-learners. Like Smiles said: "Success comes from overcoming difficulties." Marten said: "A focused and healthy goal can cure thousands of diseases." Kingsley said: "When I start doing what I do, it seems that there is nothing else to do in the world." The most thorough thing about this kind of talk is Carlyle. He said: "The abilities of creatures are different in strength and weakness, but even the weakest person, if he can concentrate all his abilities and concentrate on one thing, then, even if the ability is weak, there will be considerable success. On the contrary, a person with great ability, if he is distracted to engage in various undertakings, his result will definitely be nothing." Therefore, the constant dripping of water can penetrate huge stones; the rushing torrents will not even leave a trace afterwards. Indeed, if we study on our own without concentration and perseverance, then the final result will be like a torrent of water without a trace. Because the facts tell us that true knowledge is the fairest thing in the world. If you lack the above two spirits, even if you spend money and time to buy and expect, it will never give you unconditionally. If we have the above spirit to study on our own, not to mention the academic achievements can reach the highest peak, even if this perseverance is used in the development of the cause, it will not be of considerable help!

Shouting emptyly to demand true knowledge will never increase your practical knowledge; this is as correct as sticking a piece of paper with the four words "Bring Me Wealth" on the wall of the opposite door. Sitting and cursing the loss of past opportunities is nothing more than cursing. If we who are engaged in occupations want to acquire some true knowledge, we should strive to explore it in order to be successful.

Emerson said: "No one in the world can destroy your success except yourself." Cursing and sighing is your own destruction; truly, only focusing on hard work is a path to success.

Art World

Watched Two Dance Performances 296

— Man Yun

丨Xinhua at Jin Cheng · Fei Yan Society at Carlton丨

The dance world currently doesn't have a fixed base. They can only take advantage of seasons when film sales aren't doing well to "make a splash" in movie theaters. Near the Lunar New Year, affairs are chaotic, and the people with free time to watch movies are ultimately too few. Movie theater business inevitably suffers. Even good films are probably hard to sell for money. No foolish boss would release a good film at this time. Some simple merchandise is bound to be pushed out to "suit the occasion," so dance can also try its hand during this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. Last Lunar New Year, Xinhua at Jin Cheng and Fei Yan's debut at Carlton managed to cause a temporary sensation, which was also due to these reasons. I watched these two performances, and I want to express my admiration for their efforts and their refusal to use sensuality as a selling point. However, I cannot help but express my thoughts on the results of their performances. Now I will write down my observations.

First, I want to talk about Xinhua. Xinhua is a somewhat famous dance troupe in Shanghai. Although it hasn't been established for long, it has had several performances. This troupe has a strong "business sense." Usually, many members are involved in the film and broadcasting industries. Therefore, the arrangement of new programs is often limited by time and talent. In the past, they had brought out some simple leftovers from the Bright Moon Society to give to the audience. This time, they similarly lack new contributions. For example, the program I saw on January 25th included things like "Peach Blossom River," "Peanuts," "Fair Trade," "Farewell My Brother," "Secrets of Love," "Heart of Love," "Special Express," "Jasmine Gracious Village," "Silver River Twin Stars," etc. Needless to say, the content is empty and simple. Even the melodies are mostly outdated and difficult to give high praise (the Li-style dance is difficult to obtain high praise whether in music or dance). It is worth mentioning the several "talents" that Xinhua used to attract attention this time. I didn't see "Lei Ying Star" Wang Renmei and "Singer" Wang Manjie's "guest appearances," so I can't say anything. However, their voices probably won't disappoint the audience too much. Among the guest performers, Yuan Meiyun is a very eye-catching one. This time, I watched her collaborations with Zhou Xuan in "Jasmine Yearning for Home" and with Yan Hua in "Peach Blossom River," among other programs. People generally say that Yuan Meiyun has a lot of promise. In reality, this "bud that needs irrigation and nurturing" does indeed have performing talent. If it weren't for the excessive praise of bored people and the relationship of business sense, she would indeed have a future. Saying she is a "beautiful little bird" certainly underestimates her, and treating her as a "money tree" also seems short-sighted. A truly pure artist should refuse all unwanted invitations, and "hanging the first signboard" is only the pursuit and behavior of those who are eager for vanity and unwilling to make progress. As for the program, performing "Peach Blossom River" at this time, no matter how skilled the performance, is undoubtedly insignificant. Similarly, in "Jasmine Yearning for Home," she and Zhou Xuan both have excellent performances, but this kind of thing itself doesn't have much value. Even if it's performed well, what does that count for? In order to do a "deal," when Fei Yan Society performed at Carlton, she also collaborated with Fei Yan's Louis on "Selling Flowers" and sang "Little Jasmine" solo. Our views on these two programs are the same as above. In addition, Chen Jingfang, Jiang Manli, and others also made guest appearances in Xinhua's performances. Both of their voices have unattainable qualities, but they also have a common problem: their enunciation is not very clear, and the tunes they sing are mostly sentimental "靡靡之音" (decadent music).

Xinhua's main actress, Zhou Xuan, is a talented singer and dancer. She has a lot of talent, but unfortunately, her talent is not used very appropriately. She appeared in "Special Express" with a lively and humorous demeanor. Her role was suitable, and her performance was not bad. She played the main role in "Secrets of Love," "Light of the Nation," "Fair Trade," "Heart of Love," and "Fengyang Woman," and she was able to handle them all happily. "Fair Trade" touched on the realistic problem of unemployment, but unfortunately, it trivialized the seriousness of this problem. In "Fengyang Woman," she and Yu Hua wore colorful dance costumes and sang and danced. We couldn't see the pain of the wandering life of the Fengyang women who left their hometowns under the intertwined oppression of natural disasters and man-made calamities. This disregard for real life is a common feature of Xinhua's programs!

Fei Yan's performance at Carlton, although not as commercially successful as Xinhua, perhaps has a more progressive understanding of dance. They want to get rid of the Li-style tradition of "forest of powdered legs" and "half-exposed breasts," attempting to change the trend of the dance world with new forms and content. They use a large number of exotic programs, such as "Gypsy Dance," "Cossack Dance," "Palace Dance," "Hungarian Dance," "Naval Review," etc., which are all very eye-catching. In particular, "Gypsy Dance," with its strong rhythm and dance, and "Cossack Dance," which reveals a kind of robust appearance through its rough rhythm, can both make people feel excited and powerful. In addition, the newly compiled "Selling Cloth Ballad" also quite expresses one side of the lives of people in the lower classes. As for the "Savage Dance" performed by Xu Canying and Huang Hun, although the performance is skilled, the content of this kind of thing cannot but make people frown.

There is also one program in Fei Yan's performance that cannot be missed: the three-act dance drama "Blood and Tears on the Battlefield." Although "Blood and Tears on the Battlefield" adopted the realistic theme of volunteer soldiers resisting the enemy, this theme was destroyed by the play's inappropriate arrangement. Strictly speaking, this play is a patchwork success. There is no emotional process, no plot connection, no complete story... Even the inserted dances and songs seem to be pieced together, far-fetched and stiff.

Fei Yan has a promising future. We hope that its members can reflect, and we also hope that it can accept external criticism and establish dance art in a realm that does not anesthetize the audience and does not beautify reality. To sing of "peace and prosperity through song and dance" at this time is certainly a "chronistic error." Dance is by no means a hymn in the mouth of a pastor, nor is it an ice cream for the eyes to eat, but it must be a performance of objective reality.

Training and Cultivating a Steel Heart and Iron Will 297

— Lu Wen

"I cannot do this." The lieutenant said to Alexander in this way. At that time, the military situation was extremely tense, and the fortress had been lost. "Go forward!" The general replied: "Trying can lead to success." Finally, the dense formation moved forward and defeated the enemy.

Napoleon visited the plague victims in Egypt, and he told them that a person must not destroy his courage with fear. A willpower is like a strong tonic to the human body, which can stimulate people to complete superhuman acts. Napoleon also said: "The word 'difficult' exists only in the dictionary of fools." When we examine his life's great achievements, he never saw obstruction in the word "difficult." He always used a steel heart and iron will to overcome all difficulties.

Walter Scott was in debt for more than 60,000 yuan at the age of fifty-five. He decided that every yuan of debt must be cleared before his death. This strong determination was deeply buried in his mind, and every nerve and muscle was engraved with the idea of ​​repaying the debt. He worked hard to write articles in exchange for money, and finally all his debts were cleared. In his diary, he said: "Although I am busy all day, I must work hard to attack." This is his strong willpower.

"If ordinary people have will, there is nothing difficult. If this is needed, then it must be done; thus, one can succeed." Mirabeau once said this.

Someone said that Pitt's only plan was to "break through the difficulties." He said, "Is that difficult? I have overcome obstacles." His service and loyalty in Congress are admirable.

Darwin was a sickly child. Although he suffered frequently, his patience was admirable. His son said of him: "In four years, my father never knew a healthy day." Because in the period of forty years, he only worked constantly. He had a strange power, that is, he liked to concentrate on one thing.

De Vere has an old poem, although the words are old and decayed, its meaning is immortal. 丨丨

"Man's victory lies in sincerity, a steel heart and iron will overcome the enemy, the weak but have courage, can make defeat turn into victory."

Sunday Literary Society

How to Write Literary Works? 298

— Wang Jicong

If you are a young student or a white-collar worker who loves literature and you want to learn to write literary works, or you are writing literary works, then a question must arise in your mind: how to write? I want to discuss this question with you now, and I think this is something you would be happy to do.

First of all, if you want to write novels, poems, or dramas, you must have the technical ability to write. If you don't know how to describe emotions and scenery, and you don't have the artistic talent to portray things, you can't write literary works. But this artistic talent does not come from innate ability, but depends on your acquired cultivation. In this process, I hope you don't believe in those so-called novel or poetry writing methods that are popular on the market, because these things are mostly scams. Even if you read ten or eight books of this kind of so-called writing methods, at most you will only know some mechanical methods of making sentences and refining words, and you cannot increase your artistic talent. I think the most necessary thing for you is to read more great works by great writers, and learn the methods of description from Shakespeare, Goethe, Balzac, Flaubert, Turgenev, Gorky... melt their artistic description rules into your own description rules, and engage in literary creation. In this way, through continuous hard work in writing, your artistic talent will naturally increase day by day.

Secondly, speaking of writing, of course it is necessary to have writing material. Some people say that the subject matter is not important, natural scenery, the wealth of the rich, the suffering of the poor, the sorrow of young girls... can all be used as subject matter. The problem lies only in what viewpoint to express it from, that is, how to express it. In fact, this only sees the importance of the creative attitude; it ignores the activeness of the subject matter. Because literary works are artistically

Page 22

Reflecting social life to unite human thoughts and feelings, if the things described by the writer have a very close and obvious relationship with the lives of most social people, then its binding force on human beings in terms of thought and emotion will inevitably be great; conversely, if the writer describes things that have no direct and obvious relationship with our lives, then its moving power will be very small. For example, in present-day China, the issues that have the greatest relationship with the lives of ordinary people are the issue of imperialist aggression, natural disasters, and the decline of industry and commerce and the bankruptcy of the rural economy. If you do not find subject matter among these, or even if you do not find subject matter that has the greatest relationship with these phenomena, and you go to describe natural scenery or rare and special social phenomena, then even if you have great artistic talent, you cannot write literary works with great value that are suitable for the needs of the objective world. Therefore, in choosing subject matter, you must rely on your life experience, your feelings and observations, and use things that have the greatest relationship with our lives, the main social phenomena, and typical social life and its trends as subject matter to strive for your creation.

At the same time, your sincerity to things and the position you stand in when creating are especially important. We know that under the same subject matter, if two writers with different viewpoints are asked to create, then the social thoughts and emotions expressed will inevitably be different, and therefore their values ​​will also be different. For example, if the "January 28th" Japanese attack on China incident is used as subject matter, if a writer with a profiteering merchant's consciousness and a writer who fights for the independence of the Chinese nation are asked to write, then the content and value of the works they write will be very different. At the same time, literature likes truth, and the value of literary works is mainly determined by whether the thoughts expressed are true and to what extent. George said: "When false and incorrect thoughts lie at the root of an artistic work, then the thoughts cause internal contradictions in the work, and therefore the aesthetic value of the work will inevitably be harmed." But how can we prevent "false and incorrect thoughts from lying in the work"? How can we express the truth? This depends on your ideology, your worldview, and your position.

Naturally, when describing, you can start from the beginning of the story and write all the way down; you can also write from the end of the story to the beginning and the middle; you can also start from the middle and look back to the beginning and then expand to the future: these can all be at your convenience, depending on how the description is suitable for the story and thoughts you want to express, and you will describe it that way. However, there is one point that you must decide, that is, you must not narrate flatly or preach abstractly, you must describe it concretely and vividly. For the expression of the characters' emotions and for the development of things, you must grasp their concrete dynamics to describe them, and you must not make abstract preaching under the law of tranquility. In Guyau's "Art from a Sociological Perspective," there are these sentences:

"Your tone is more beautiful than your voice,

Your smile is more lovely than your lips,

Your eyes are better than your eyes,

Its brilliance, no fire has such a flame."

Why is this? Because moving postures are more stimulating to the senses and more eye-catching than static shapes. In artistic expression, vivid descriptions have a greater artistic power to move people than calm narratives.

Finally, the so-called artistic talent, the so-called choice of subject matter, the so-called position, and the so-called description rules are all closely related to your life. Therefore, you must live earnestly and have rich life experience to write literary works. Sometimes, practical investigation and experience of various social lives are also necessary for you. Tolstoy criticized Turgenev, saying, "You only know life from newspapers," of course, he meant that you should actually investigate life; Zola had to visit the characters he wanted to portray and investigate the life he wanted to express before writing... It is indeed very necessary to actually investigate and experience life like this sometimes. Because some social lives cannot be understood without actual experience, and naturally they cannot be described. Therefore, in order to create, in addition to living earnestly in your living environment, you should also go to the general public to enrich your life experience and knowledge.

Postscript on "Under the Mercury Lamp" and "Song of Spring" 300

— Shi Ying

In this year of theatrical silence, the performance of the two plays "Under the Mercury Lamp" and "Song of Spring" can be regarded as a noteworthy event. In addition to admiring the perseverance and enthusiasm of the gentlemen of the Shanghai Stage Association for drama, we also want to say a few words about the content and performance of these two plays:

㈠ "Under the Mercury Lamp"

"Under the Mercury Lamp" is a play that takes its material from the real life of the film industry. It not only shows the different tasks of film practitioners in the process of film production, but also portrays their unique feelings and personalities based on their different positions. This place even puts special emphasis on the latter point, describing the unbearable aspects of the working lives of senior film practitioners, such as managers, directors, stage managers, set designers, photographers, sound engineers, big stars... and the depravity of life, the superficiality of knowledge and learning... All the various forms in the "dark circle" are objectively recorded here with a hint of satire. The difficult experiences of some lower-level employees, especially extras, and their courage to fight against life are also vividly portrayed here.

The plot of this play is very simple, it is just a record of a true image under the mercury lamp and the adventure and patriotic enthusiasm of an extra. The hardship and hard work of the extras, the humiliation and molestation of female extras by senior personnel are inserted here and are important themes used here; but what is more important is the encounter of the extra C 丨 丨 a person who failed to resist the enemy in the Northeast and returned to Shanghai, and only works as an extra to make a living 丨 丨 and his wife who became a female star, as well as his enthusiasm for resisting the enemy. He rebuked his wife who sold her soul. He did not listen to the director's instructions. In the scene of retreating, he replaced it with advancing. The heroic national war in the Northeast swayed in his memory, arousing his passionate and forward emotions. In this age of forgetfulness, such subject matter can undoubtedly evoke our painful memories.

The production technique of this play is generally good, but there are also some minor problems. For the sake of space, I don't want to say how tight its structure is, how vivid its character is, and how humorous its dialogue is... I just want to review a little bit of its flaws. I think the chance encounter between the extra C and his wife is a bit "no coincidence, no play". Even if this kind of thing is quite possible, it seems that the playwright did not properly expose it in advance, and it is difficult to make people believe it deeply.

The performance of the actors, because those who appear on stage are all experienced people, the results will certainly not disappoint people. Speaking of personal achievements, the director of Wan Laitian, the male and female stars of Zheng Junli and Hu Ping, and the extra C of Yuan Muzhi are all worth mentioning.

㈡ "Song of Spring"

"Song of Spring" is a very moving play. There are tragic and fierce scenes here, typical character descriptions, and generous and sorrowful dirges. There is a kind of passionate enthusiasm, calm courage, and determination to sacrifice, which covers this "Song of Spring" with a layer of tragic and heavy mist.

The plot is not that complicated, it just describes the heroic experience and unfortunate encounter of three young educators who ran back to the motherland from Nanyang to join the Volunteer Army. The first act writes about their life in Nanyang and their indignation at the fall of the Northeast. The characteristics of the male and female protagonists and the depth of their private relationship are also well explained in the first act. A kind of deep friendship is also inserted through two supporting roles. The difficulties of the Nanyang Chinese in starting a business, their current mistreatment by the local government, and the economic crisis in Nanyang are all briefly mentioned in the mouths of the actors. In the second act, the male protagonist Wei Han and his friends Si Xun and Bi Ru did not make it to the Northeast, but they achieved their desire to serve the motherland in the "January 28th" war in Shanghai. The stage is set with the scene of a wounded soldier hospital run by overseas Chinese. Here we see the groans of some respectable wounded soldiers, the diagnosis and treatment of admirable doctors, the care of young ladies, and the admirable and great enthusiasm of the people for resisting the enemy. Everything is a magnificent reenactment of the enthusiasm of the people in the rear during the "January 28th" period to resist the enemy. In the third act, Wei Han was injured and became an idiot; but because of the sound of firecrackers on this New Year's Day, it aroused his tragic memories of charging, and he recovered his neurological health in this memory.

The general outline of the whole play is roughly like this. The unattainable aspect of this play is that the subject matter is true, especially the fact that it is closely linked with the current crisis of our nation and the bright prospects of its future. Although there are still some accidental coincidences in the writing technique, on the whole, this play is worth seeing.

The actors are almost all All-Star Cast. Due to long-term training and excellent guidance from the host, the performance results can generally be said to be good. The personal achievements of the actors are excellent, including Wang Renmei, Wang Ying, Zhao Dan, Mei Xi, Jin Yan, and Wei Helin.

Seasonal Articles

Year-End of the Abandoned Calendar in My Hometown 301

— Jia Yu

The days grew longer after the "Winter Solstice". The ship I was on docked at the Jiujiang wharf, and the sun was still a bright red, hanging high in the sky, reflecting in the river, creating colorful rays like shimmering fish scales.

The day the ship arrived happened to be the morning of the abandoned calendar's New Year's Eve. The ship was full of passengers like me, returning home for the New Year (?). On everyone's face, you could see the joy that came from the heart, and the ship was filled with pleasant air.

As the ship approached the "pontoon," still a dozen feet away, the porters standing on the "pontoon" seemed to be desperate for food. They leapt onto the ship one by one, like eagles pouncing on their prey; their movements were as quick as arrows, and they were upon you before you could blink.

Watching this kind of competition for survival, I felt a little scared. Good heavens! A distance of more than ten feet – if one were to slip, would one survive? I wondered.

After all, the issue of eating was more serious than any other. Therefore, what I was thinking perhaps didn't even exist in their minds. So, before the ship was properly docked at the "pontoon," they had already jumped aboard, some even finding customers.

I was in the rear cabin, and the porters hadn't reached there yet. The steward bundled up my luggage and placed it on the berth, telling me to wait by the side door.

He said, "Sir, don't wander off. This wharf is worse than others. If you look away for a moment, your things will be stolen."

"Thank you, I know!" I smiled at him.

At this moment, three or four porters rushed in from the front cabin. Each held a carrying pole made of half a bamboo, with two hemp rope "pads" the size of copper gongs hanging from it. This was their entire "livelihood" for making a living.

"Sir! Are you going to the city? I'll carry it for you, cheap!" A porter, appearing familiar, walked into my cabin and lifted the bedding.

"Put it down! We'll agree on the price before you move anything!" I glared at him.

He suddenly felt a sense of surprise, his body trembled slightly, and he took two steps back, a look of disappointment immediately surfacing on his face. He never expected that I would be from Jiujiang!

"Sir! Easy, easy; we're from the same hometown, would I overcharge you?" he said with a forced smile.

"No, it's best to agree on it first. How much to carry it into the city?" I pretended to be an experienced traveler.

"Sir, we're from the same hometown, no 'empty talk,' let's say five jiao!" he said, stretching out a thick arm, looking very determined.

"Five jiao? "I glanced at the porters behind him, thinking that surely one or two of them would automatically lower the price.

"Five jiao, truly not cheating you, sir!" he quickly added before the other porters could speak.

"Not cheating? Nonsense! I used to pay others at most one jiao, and you're saying five, huh!"

"One jiao? You can't get anyone to carry it for that price anymore! Sir, you don't know how hard it is to carry things now. Even with five jiao for carrying a load, it's not enough to eat. You, sir, are involved in big money, you don't know our hardships! If you, sir, want someone to carry it, honestly, let's say four jiao!" An older porter standing behind him chimed in, explaining at length.

I was getting a little impatient, and I quickly interrupted him, saying, "Fine, it's three jiao, I won't pay you a single copper more!"

The porters looked at each other, all silently focusing their gaze on me.

"What do you say? Hurry up and speak!" I urged them.

"You carry it for him, okay?" The older porter, with a look of disappointment, said to the porter who had spoken first.

This was my first time returning home for the "New Year" in five years. The bedding and suitcase were still the same two items I had when I left, but now they were even more worn out. The two items rested on the porter's shoulder, as light as two bundles of torn cotton, swaying back and forth as he walked.

"Three jiao, to carry it to the city, really cheap," I heard the old porter say as I walked onto the deck.

The porter and I walked from the wharf to "Zheng Street." This hometown street, which I hadn't seen in five years, had aged with the ruthless passage of time!

Although some of the shops on both sides were equipped with wireless radios like those in Shanghai, as a way to attract customers, the number of people who could actually go in and buy things was few enough to count. This desolate scene was absolutely unheard of on New Year's Eve of the abandoned calendar five years ago!

When I arrived home, two tables had already been placed together in the middle of the parlor, neatly arranged with the "three sacrificial animals." In front of the table was a large brazier, burning bright red charcoal. The crackling sound of the exploding charcoal was like the sound of firecrackers. This was probably in preparation for "Returning Blessings."

In this parlor where my shadow had disappeared for five years, I suddenly reappeared. No wonder my mother was so stunned at the time that she couldn't speak for a long time. Her entire heart was covered with this unexpected joy. Her aging face was filled with smiles, as if she had made a great fortune. She was so happy that she even forgot to prepare the New Year's Eve meal for the offerings.

The people at home all hoped for me to return like this. However, what could I bring to comfort them? Five years of wandering had deprived me of my inherent innocence and simplicity, and had severed my emotional connection with my family. During these long five years, the shadow of my family had gradually faded in my mind with the passing days, and even the faintest impression was gone! However, they were still as kind and sincere to me as they had been in the past. Perhaps my return this time would add a lot of interest to the New Year they were celebrating!

I stared blankly at the "Returning Blessings" offerings on the table for a while, and my mother thought I was tired from the boat and feeling unwell. She quickly reached out and touched my cheeks, asking me with concern, "Ju'er! What's wrong, are you feeling uncomfortable anywhere? Huh?"

"Nothing! I see that there's 'real chicken' for 'Returning Blessings' on the table this year. I find that very strange!" I said, smiling at my mother.

"Oh!" Mother thought she understood what I meant, and a look of relief surfaced on her face. Then, she told me the reason for using "real chicken" for "Returning Blessings" this year. She said, "Ju'er! You don't know, this year the price of chicken is almost the same as fake chicken! Radishes! Almost the same, one dollar buys ten-plus jin, and they're big, fat hens! Hey! Country people usually hold chickens in their hands, shouting 'one dollar for twelve jin,' and no one wants them. These past few days, as New Year's is approaching, they're only selling for one dollar for ten jin. I'm lucky I bought them early, otherwise I would have lost out!" Mother said, sighing.

"One dollar for ten jin of chicken? That's practically like eating chicken as rice!" I couldn't quite believe that my mother's words were definitely reliable.

"Eating it as rice? Can't be done! Country people still need rice!" Mother retorted.

I was supposed to burn incense and kowtow for "Returning Blessings" this year. Although I was full of reluctance, there was no way to refuse. After a while, all the cooked dishes for the New Year's Eve dinner were brought out, and the table was so full that there was no room to place the wine cups. Later, there were a few bowls that really couldn't fit, so I told them to take them back. However, Mother was a little unwilling, as if she was complaining that I hadn't burned incense and kowtowed when "Returning Blessings" at home in the past five years, and that I still wasn't sincere this time?

That evening's New Year's Eve dinner was a very happy one for everyone. Mother, needless to say, was even happier because I would be spending the New Year at home this year. She usually didn't drink much wine, but tonight she made an exception and had two cups. Later, my sister was afraid that she would get drunk, so she didn't pour her any more.

"Ju'er! If you come back for the New Year again next year, I don't know how happy Mother will be!" my sister said, looking at my mother, whose face was full of smiles.

"Hmm!" I just smiled slightly; I really didn't dare to guarantee that I would be able to come back next year, so I just gave a perfunctory response.

However, Mother had great hopes. She said in a commanding tone, "Of course you have to come back for the New Year next year. Where's the sense in leaving home for years and not coming back, forgetting even your family? As the saying goes, 'A tree may grow a thousand feet tall, but its leaves return to the roots.' If you don't come back usually, you should always come back for the New Year! 'With money or without money, come home for the New Year.' Look at Third Uncle of the Big House in front, he's so far away in Beiping, but he still rushes back for the New Year!"

"With money or without money, come home for the New Year." I understood what Mother meant by saying this. She was afraid that I would be too embarrassed to come back if I didn't have money, so she encouraged me that the family would always welcome me even if I didn't have money. However, my thinking was exactly the opposite of hers; I felt that if I didn't have money, there was no need to celebrate the New Year, and that with money, every day was like celebrating the New Year. I still didn't know what changes my life and future would bring next year, so I couldn't guarantee whether I would be able to go back for the New Year!

Famous Quotes

Zheng Banqiao's Sayings 302

— Chong Shi

Zheng Banqiao is one of the past literary figures that I particularly admire. I like his free and unrestrained character, his unconventional behavior, and also his unique style of painting orchids and bamboos and his calligraphy. Although he was just an ordinary bureaucrat in his middle age, having lost the fresh temperament of his youth, he was still a person capable of writing well and cultivating moral character. His words of wisdom on reading, learning, and conducting oneself are still worth our emulating. I have read many of his family letters in my spare time, and I have now excerpted some of his wise sayings for our discerning readers to use as a reference:

Reading should be diligent and not lax, and reading books should be careful and constant.

For important points, take notes in a reading diary; for points that are difficult to understand, write them down on a separate piece of paper and seek clarification from a teacher.

When reading a book and encountering sentences that are useful in practice, they should be recorded immediately; if they can be categorized and compiled into a large volume, they can be used as material for writing, and the benefits are endless.

Governing is not about much talking, and neither is learning.

When people study, they cannot be sure of achieving success, but even if they do not achieve success, they must study. Set your mind on it. If fame does not come, knowledge remains with me, and it is not a losing proposition.

The most important thing in writing is to be calm and incisive, as in the *Zuo Zhuan*, *Shi Ji*, Zhuangzi, Lisao, Du Fu's poems, and Han Yu's prose.

To be able to recite a book after reading it once is not the most effective way. To understand with the eyes but be hasty in the mind, with little room in the heart and unable to cope with the constant flow, is like looking at a beautiful woman in a theater, glancing once and passing her by, what does it have to do with me?

Rather than making indiscriminate friends and incurring losses, it is better to be isolated and ignorant.

If people are seen as lovable, then I am also lovable; if people are seen as detestable, then I am also detestable.

When it comes to writing and scholarship, people often think they are superior and that success is within easy reach, but they are all just taking chances.

I have never liked keeping birds in cages. I seek pleasure, but they are in prison; what kind of feeling or reason is it to bend the nature of things to suit my own nature?

A gentleman who studies the Way loves others, governs with a broad vision, and does not advocate overcorrection.

There are five ways to maintain health: (1) Get up early at dawn and eat a bowl of plain porridge, without any side dishes; (2) Take a walk after meals, aiming for a thousand steps; (3) Meditate at a fixed time, sitting quietly for a while after school each day; (4) Do not get annoyed or angry when encountering things; (5) Do not think after going to bed.

Book and Magazine Reviews

Reading "New Life" Volumes One, Numbers Forty-Eight and Forty-Nine 303

— Ji Chong

丨Published by New Life Weekly, priced at four cents per copy丨

"New Life" is currently the most popular little publication among ordinary progressive small and medium-sized clerks and young students in China. It is said to have already had five or six thousand readers. This is naturally very "special" in the current situation of the general book industry downturn and in the year of "magazine competition". However, this special situation is not caused by the "special" distribution methods of the "New Life" publishers, but by its good content. I am a regular reader of "New Life". Now I will write down my feelings after reading the "New Life" in the forty-eighth and forty-ninth issues of Volume One, so that readers can know a general outline of this publication.

Lying is annoying, and truth is lovely. "New Life" tells the truth, so it can gain the love of a wide range of readers. It bravely approaches reality, observes with fair and scientific eyes, and vividly reveals its true posture. For example, Bi Yuncheng's "Distribution of American Wealth" in issue 48 truly expresses the extremely unequal essence of the gilded kingdom of gold that our gilded doctors yearn for; and Yi Shui's "Decline of Gandhism" and Xing Su's "Thoughts on Reading Newspapers" in issue 49 both tell us truthfully about the decline of Gandhism in India and the faces of the gentlemen. 丨丨Boldly speaking "honest words" is the first characteristic of "New Life".

Second, "New Life" does not rummage through China's old wastepaper baskets, nor does it transport foreign antiques. What it talks about are all realistic issues that are closely related to our lives. For example, Kan Ru's "Dong Shi Imitating Xi Shi", Fang Yin's "People Who Joke with Peace", Yu Zhen's "What is the Biggest Enemy of Women?" and Ge Qiao's "The Third Reich with Latent Internal Worries" (issue 48) and "The Reef of the Baltic Sea 丨丨Memel" (issue 49) are all talking about realistic Chinese or world issues. Among them, "Dong Shi Imitating Xi Shi" expresses the ugliness of all imperialists, the enemies of our nation; "People Who Joke with Peace" says that the minions of the God of War, Henderson (chairman of the disarmament conference), Briand (the deceased French Foreign Minister), and Sir Austen Chamberlain (a major shareholder of the British Vickers arms factory), have all received the Nobel Peace Prize; "What is the Biggest Enemy of Women?" warns and satirizes those "new women" who only pay attention to formal, inconsistent words and deeds. The author made this powerful warning at the end: "The road is long, it does not need empty talk but needs to be walked down step by step. If even naturally big feet want to pretend to be like the vile and stinky three-inch golden lotuses, then it is the most shameful expression of slavishness, and this slavishness is the biggest enemy of women."; "The Third Reich with Latent Internal Worries" and "The Reef of the Baltic Sea 丨丨Memel" scientifically analyze the two international issues that are closely related to the current world crisis.

Third, in addition to publishing opinions that are closely related to our lives, "New Life" also publishes things that describe the lives of various professions and the situations in various places. Cheng Heqiu's "Looking at the Iron Industry in the World War Again", Lu Xinqiu's "From Jiangnan to Qingdao" in issue 48, and Wei Chuan's "Trainees in the Electric Light Company" in issue 49, etc., are not only texts of true life sketches, but also good materials for literary writers and good materials for studying social problems.

Fourth, "New Life" not only truly expresses reality and explains life, but also properly tells us how we should live and encourages us to move forward. For example, Bi Yuncheng in issue 49 tells us: "The attitude of doing things that is expressed by holding a decadent mentality is the most undesirable attitude of doing things"; "dissatisfied with reality and demanding progress", "but the methods adopted are clamorous and disorderly, and only show their temper", "this attitude of doing things that is expressed by holding a impetuous mentality", "is also not desirable"; "dissatisfied with the status quo, strive to understand the root causes of social ills", "strive to make the goal correct, and strive to understand the fundamental principles of human social survival and evolution", "This attitude of doing things that is expressed by holding a calm and struggling mentality", "is "worthy of being an example for ordinary people"! 丨丨This is indeed the right attitude to life, the right way of life.

Fifth, although the position of "New Life" is a scientific position, the language used to express opinions is very popular and interesting. There are no stiff "New Life Jargon" such as "opening up", "twisting", etc., nor are there upside-down Westernized phrases. All of them are very popular, lively, and generous articles. Among them, general essays, sketches, and life sketches are of course popular and beautiful, and even hard political and economic articles are extremely vivid and lively. For example, Mofu's "A Year-Long China Economic Tour" in issue 49 is a "hard" economic paper, but we can be very interested in reading it. The author did not use dry and tasteless statistical tables to explain China's economy in the past year, but used the suffering of farmers, the lives of workers, the situation of banks and shops, and the necessary figures to explain it, so that people feel that what is said in it has a major relationship with their own lives, which is completely different from the situation when reading those economic papers that specialize in using statistical tables to scare people.

Sixth, "New Life" is very responsible for general readers. Whenever her readers ask her questions, she can patiently and carefully give them proper explanations. I think the "Readers' Correspondence Column" of "New Life" is better than all kinds of small publications in the country: this may also be one of the main reasons why she can grab readers.

Finally, in addition to introducing "New Life" to everyone, we also hope that "New Life" will be further enriched in the future. In my personal opinion, "New Life" still lacks texts on the theories of various academics and the methods of studying social problems, and these kinds of things are currently urgently needed by ordinary young people in China, and the "New Life" that is loved by a wide range of readers seems to meet their needs.

Einstein's Biography (3) 308

— From Wood

At the beginning of 1903, Einstein married Mileva Marić, a former classmate from Zurich. At this time, his close friends included Besso, Maurice Solovine, and the young mathematician Konrad Habicht. These friends often spent entire nights at his home discussing scientific and philosophical issues. Sometimes, when they became excited, they would talk loudly, which disturbed others' sleep, often leading to disputes with him.

In 1904, his wife gave birth to a son, who was also named Albert. From this year, the most productive academic period of Einstein's life began.

During this time, apart from his service at the Patent Office, Einstein devoted the rest of his time to family matters and academic pursuits. This can be said to be the beginning of his profound research.

His earliest paper, published in the "Annalen der Physik" (one of Germany's leading academic journals for over a century), was the paper "On a Heuristic Point of View Concerning the Production and Transformation of Light," published in this journal in 1901. Subsequently, in 1902, 1903, and 1904, the journal published a total of four articles by him, all concerning thermodynamics, molecular theory, and the new statistical mechanics.

The four papers published in the "Annalen der Physik" in 1905 all have immortal value. They can be said to be epoch-making studies in the three different aspects that constitute physics. From then on, Einstein's academic position was established, but it still took time for the general public to recognize it.

Among these four papers, the first to be published, which appeared on March 17th, was the paper "On a Heuristic Point of View Concerning the Production and Transformation of Light." This was based on the so-called quantum theory of light, extending Planck's quantum hypothesis, derived in 1900 on the theory of thermal radiation, beyond thermal radiation to phenomena such as luminescence. It also records the basic relationship of the photoelectric effect, which was later widely used, the so-called Einstein equation.

The paper "On the Movement of Small Particles Suspended in Stationary Liquids Required by the Molecular-Kinetic Theory of Heat," published on May 11th, discusses the so-called Brownian motion, based on his years of research in the molecular theory of thermodynamics.

Up to this point, Einstein's published papers were all about thermodynamics and molecular theory. The paper "On the Production and Transformation of Light" was also based on the consideration of the molecular theory of thermodynamics. However, the paper "On the Electrodynamics of Moving Bodies," published in June 1905, was completely different. This was about other fields of physics. Ten years later, he published his famous general theory of relativity, the precursor of what is now called the special theory of relativity. As for his fourth article, published in the "Annalen der Physik" in 1905, entitled "Does the Inertia of a Body Depend Upon Its Energy-Content?", it should be viewed as a continuation of the third article mentioned above.

In 1905, he also submitted a thesis to Professor Alfred Kleiner at the University of Zurich and obtained a doctorate. This thesis was published in the "Annalen der Physik" in 1906 under the title "A New Determination of Molecular Dimensions."

Because Einstein obtained a doctorate, Professor Kleiner felt it necessary to invite this excellent young scholar to the University of Zurich. However, he could not immediately become a university professor and had to work as a temporary lecturer. The income of a lecturer was not enough to support his family, so he was very embarrassed at the time. Fortunately, there was also a university in Bern, so he stayed in Bern, still maintaining his position at the Patent Office, while also serving as a lecturer at the University of Bern.

At that time, only two people were officially registered as listeners to Einstein's lectures. One was Besso mentioned above, and the other was Schapp, a young technician from the Telecommunications Bureau. Both of them were originally capable. However, it is regrettable that Einstein encountered such a situation in his first appearance. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Dolores Del Rio's Way to a Happy Family 313

— Xilin

Dolores Del Rio's personal intelligence, calmness, bravery, and the fulfillment of her family life have become a well-praised story in Hollywood. When many young women among Hollywood stars encounter family changes and marital discord, they ask Dolores Del Rio for advice. Therefore, Dolores Del Rio is very qualified to say a few words about the issue of how to achieve a happy family.

Although she is not very old, she is a person with a rich mind and keen observation, whether in times of success or failure. Her commitment to building a happy family is also where she has thought and intelligence. She said: "Simply put, when you plan something, whether that thing is important or trivial, you always have to think about the possibility of failure, and prepare a secondary plan to maintain your position, to comfort you, and to encourage you after your first plan fails. That is the retreat you leave for yourself. No matter who or what, a retreat is indispensable."

Now let's take a very small thing as an example. For example, one night, you plan to go out for dinner and see a movie after dinner. Suddenly your friend, or your husband, comes back and obviously doesn't want to go out because he is tired. If you had left a retreat when planning to go out, preparing for the possibility that going out wouldn't be successful, then your disappointment would naturally be reduced a lot, and you wouldn't get angry.

This is a small thing, but the small can also be used to represent the big. More important things are also like this. Taking my personal life as an example, after I have gained many lessons from hardship and difficulty, I have also planned two major roads for my lifelong career. One goes to the right, and one goes to the left. If my work on the screen fails, I will retreat from the road on the right and turn to the road on the left. That road on the left is the road back to my family life. Although I have a considerable position on the screen, it is still not satisfactory, so I am also working hard on the road on the left to prepare my retreat. My family, my gardening, my way of life, and the life of shared joys and hardships with my husband are always in my consideration. Screen life used to be excellent for me. Once it disappoints me, I will retreat and return to my family, and I won't be heartbroken.

A female star, who can think about the future retreat when her career is at its peak, and devote herself to the arrangement of the family, thinking of it as a precaution, that kind of meticulousness in thought is worthy of our admiration.

But her thinking also has unique aspects, which are unattainable by ordinary romantic female stars. That is, she agrees that after a woman gets a husband, she must be able to keep her husband. Her method of keeping her husband is not like planning something, leaving a retreat in advance, so that if this man is not suitable, she can immediately retreat and change to another one. She said very politely that she,

is a Latin race person who grew up in an old-fashioned family. Although on the one hand, she admires the freedom of modern women to choose husbands and change husbands, her own mind is inevitably a bit old-fashioned. However, when losing a husband, although there is hope of changing to a new husband, there is also considerable pain. It is better to be able to keep him without losing him. The following are the methods of keeping a husband indicated by Dolores Del Rio:

Dolores said: "Of course, I can't say which thing is the most important, but generally speaking, a married person must remember that the marriage ceremony is not the end of something, nor does it give you ownership, so that you have a natural right to that thing without having to worry about losing it. On the contrary, all the things before the wedding must continue after the wedding. The way a man gets a woman is the same as the way a woman gets a man. How you get them is how you have to keep them. The way of courtship must continue after marriage. Tenderness, consideration, understanding, and romance are all indispensable after marriage as they were before marriage. Don't let romance die after marriage. Don't regard the relationship between husband and wife as something natural that doesn't need to be considered."

"Going a step further, after marriage, husband and wife should seek a stronger union. On the woman's side, she should be proud to be able to manage the family, and she should regard family life as a precious and great career. Furthermore, household expenses should be within the scope of income. Don't develop extravagant and wasteful habits. Debt is especially something that women should not do. The method of buying things and paying in installments is the dangerous beginning of debt, which will often make you feel uneasy. So, it's better to find ways to avoid it from the beginning."

"Furthermore, after a woman marries a husband, she has the responsibility of having children. Personally, when I am ready to have children in the future, I would rather give up my career and devote myself to raising my children. A child is worth the wholehearted care of any mother. With children, the family will be more complete, and the relationship between husband and wife will be deeper. In addition, to reiterate, you must leave a retreat everywhere. Gentleness and submission are the duties of women, although you don't necessarily have to rely on men. If you can do all of the above, the husband will not easily leave his wife."

Film Review

Review of "Orchid in the Empty Valley" 丨 New Light Screening 丨 314

— Ji Han

When films are used entirely as educational tools, film authors are by no means trying to cater to the audience, but are firmly grasping the audience's needs to improve their understanding. But when films are valued entirely from a business perspective, what the film authors want to do is to lower the standard to cater to the desires of backward people. Therefore, because Hu Die can still take the lead, and because people generally love ethical films, after "Sister Flowers" and "Rebirth Flower" came this "Orchid in the Empty Valley," in which Hu Die plays three roles alone. Moreover, this outdated ethical film was once a sensation in the silent film era.

Regardless of whether a bit of revolutionary history and the bright road are added to the front or the back, the characters and stories shown here are always bizarre, tortuous, and unreasonable. I don't understand why the character played by Gao Zhanfei would participate in the Northern Expedition? And why would he lead a noble life with nothing to do after the Northern Expedition? I also don't understand why the character played by Hu Die can live with her father? ····· Everything is an unreasonable hodgepodge, an unreasonable coincidence. However, because these are all so-called dramatic plots, plus two trains playfully colliding with each other, Liang Yan's mother appears as Mrs. Li Youlan, the so-called stepmother abuses the son of the former wife, and the biological mother sees her son suffering, the so-called ethical relationship that is hard to put together is like "Sister Flowers" and other films that provoke tears from the audience for no reason.

Speaking of the screenwriting and directing techniques of "Orchid in the Empty Valley," they are also not brilliant. The story is so long and expressed in such a tedious way. It doesn't have the story of a play, it's a tedious narration, and the places where there is a play to be made are not long enough. It can't be tightened a bit to show the artistic effectiveness of film drama. For example, the scene where Shen Jun, the child, cried out for his mother in front of his mother's remains was pulled so long that all the tragic emotion was destroyed. In addition, Hu Die's pursuit of Yan Yuexian, until she grabbed the medicine bottle and revealed her true face, also lost the tense atmosphere because it was too long.

Other things, such as Gao Zhanfei going home and the servant shouting "Young master is back," are also too lengthy. Plus, the interlude of Shuang Miyue and several songs are all superfluous because they are stiff, not to mention that the creation of the songs is so naive.

As for the actors, Gao Zhanfei's beard is as ridiculously fake as Wang Xianzhai's. However, the fact that he didn't know why Yan Yuexian would commit suicide, so why did he run so fast, proves that he was mostly tired by the director. Hu Die is still the same as before, without any progress. The better one is still Yan Yuexian, who is quite vivid. In addition, such as the stiffness of the dialogue, the lack of emotion when speaking each word, and the falseness and waste of the scenery, need not be pointed out one by one.

Review of "Congratulations on Getting Rich" 315

— Ling He

Kid Millions 丨 Great Shanghai Screening

Naturally, we can't say that an actor also has his own style, but some actors have many directors or screenwriters who make films for him. Eddie Cantor has always been the consistent lead in completely imaginary films that are lively and ridiculous in form, such as "Whoopee!", such as "Roman Scandals," all of which are like this, all the way to the current "Congratulations on Getting Rich."

We can't say that "Congratulations on Getting Rich" has no content. Its content is that a poor boy accidentally gets rich, which is ridiculous, allowing people to escape from reality into a dream world of fantasy. This effect is not accidental. Later, opening an ice cream shop teaches poor boys to eat their fill. Of course, this place is exactly where a large number of people who enjoy entertainment can go to have fun. During the New Year, amid the laughter of congratulations on getting rich, many people are laughing heartily because of this. Our evaluation of this film, in addition to explaining its business role, is that there is no way to find its film art value. As for studying its director or other technical aspects, we also have nothing to say. In fact, all aspects show its mediocrity, without any characteristics.

My Review of "New Woman" 316

— Zhengyan

We cannot but say that the film "New Woman" is realistic and a work above the horizontal line.

The playwright created three different women in this film, representing three different female archetypes in the current society: one is immersed in the evil habits of luxury and licentiousness, without sound thoughts and knowledge; one is although she has new thoughts, but in reality, she lacks rational judgment, which makes the environment hinder the road she should take, and makes her unable to extricate herself; one is who has a healthy physique, a firm will, and judgment, and can resolve to implement the "do".

Among the three women of these three different forms, of course, A Ying is the new female archetype of the current society in "New Woman". This is what we cannot deny as the author's kind of progressive thinking and a lot of painstaking enlightenment.

But in terms of the structure of the content, there are many places that I think still need to be discussed: for example, since A Ying is the new woman in this film, why is she portrayed so lightly here? At the same time, A Ying's courage and hard work should of course have her own kind of difficult situation, but this is also neglected here. Also, after Wei Ming took poison, the city newspapers published the news of her death, the bookstore manager held a memorial service for her, but she was sent to the hospital, and the doctor was able to clear her poison······ These are obviously inconsistent with the facts. There are other loopholes, but I won't point them out one by one.

Director Cai Chusheng is more regressive than "Song of the Fishermen". In terms of actors, Ruan Lingyu's expression is very moving, and Chen Sujuan's performance is also very talented.

Film Novel

Remnants of a Piece of Flesh (David Copperfield) (4) 317

— Willow Village

After David tearfully bid farewell to the Micawber family, he planned his escape. He suddenly remembered that his mother and Peggotty had mentioned he had an eccentric old aunt named Betsey Trotwood. That aunt had visited his home on the stormy night of his birth. He remembered she lived in Dover, and from what he'd heard, she was a very strange old lady, but regardless, she was still his blood relative and wouldn't treat him more cruelly than others.

Having decided on his plan, the young boy set out on a long journey, the experiences of which he would never forget. He was robbed, encountered violence, was beaten, had no bed to sleep in at night, and nothing to eat during the day. Finally, after enduring countless hardships, he arrived in Dover. Exhausted and hungry, he stumbled to his Aunt Betsey's house. His aunt listened in surprise as he recounted his short and miserable life. After listening quietly, she felt a pang of compassion. She and Mr. Dick, an equally eccentric distant relative, began planning David's future.

In the short time that followed, David began to feel some joy. His aunt, though her appearance was stern and formidable, was sincere at heart. She had a peculiar habit of hating donkeys. Anyone who dared drive a donkey onto the grass in front of her door would surely be scolded and chased away by her. Therefore, the children who drove donkeys were all afraid of her. But she not only scared away the children who drove donkeys, she also scared away Mr. and Miss Murdstone. They heard David was in Dover and came to take him away, but encountered this stubborn old lady and were humiliated and left.

From then on, David was forever free from the control of his stepfather, and through his aunt's efforts, he was sent to the home of Mr. Wickfield in Canterbury. He was a friend and lawyer of his aunt's. In the Wickfield household, he not only found a peaceful, lovely, and happy home, he also met a girl of similar age to play with. She was Mr. Wickfield's child, named Agnes. Her mother had died, and although she depended on her father, she often felt lonely and isolated. Therefore, David's arrival made them feel like they had known each other for a long time.

But within the Wickfield family, all was not without its pitfalls. There was a despicable little man there named Uriah Heep. He was the evil spirit in their lives, but David did not fully understand this at first, because he was too young to perceive Mr. Wickfield's weakness. Since the death of his wife, he had become addicted to wine. Uriah was a treacherous and scheming person. He had a humble appearance, but harbored sinister intentions. He gradually took control of Wickfield's business. Uriah was nominally Wickfield's student, studying law with him, but in reality, he overstepped the bounds of a student.

Although David did not know the extent of Uriah Heep's machinations, he felt a sense of disgust the moment he saw him. His hands were soft and clammy. His expression was excessively obsequious. His face gave him nightmares. His soft, damp hands seemed to be forever resting on his shoulders.

Year after year passed in this way. David had been sent to school to study. He soon became a handsome and elegant young man. He was also talented in writing and considered pursuing a career in writing. But he lacked one thing. He had no discernment, and he did not realize that Agnes loved him. If he had known sooner, perhaps Agnes would not have wasted away for him for so many years. He was now a grown man, and the world was unfolding before him. His eyes soon turned to London, and he abandoned the happiness he could have had without seeking it in his family home. (To be continued)
